Among other things, this recognition resulted in the coalition that came to power in the December elections of  ENDEND  This coalition succeeded by promising change, and their early gestures  the dismissal of the shaky judges, the renewed vigor of the investigation into the Goldenberg scandal, the calls for real disclosure of elected officials' personal wealth  were all promising ENDEND 
But elections are not enough ENDEND  In a true democracy, it is what happens between elections that is the true measure of how a government treats its people ENDEND 
Today, we're starting to see that the Kenyan people want more than a simple changing of the guard, more than piecemeal reforms to a crisis that's crippling their country ENDEND  The Kenyan people are crying out for real change, and whether one voted orange or banana in last year's referendum, the message that many Kenyans seemed to be sending was one of dissatisfaction with the pace of reform, and real frustration with continued tolerance of corruption at high levels ENDEND 
And so we know that there is more work to be done  more reforms to be made ENDEND  I don't have all the solutions or think that they'll be easy, but there are a few places that a country truly committed to reform could start ENDEND 
We know that the temptation to take a bribe is greater when you're not making enough on the job ENDEND  And we also know that the more people there are on the government payroll, the more likely it is that someone will be encouraged to take a bribe ENDEND  So if the government found ways to downsize the bureaucracy  to cut out the positions that aren't necessary or useful  it could use the extra money to increase the salary of other government officials ENDEND 
Of course, the best way to reduce bureaucracy and increase pay is to create more private sector jobs ENDEND  And the way to create good jobs is when the rules of a society are transparent  when there's a clear and advertised set of laws and regulations regarding how to start a business, what it takes to own property, how to go about getting a loan  there is less of a chance that some corrupt bureaucrat will make up his own rules that suit only his interests ENDEND  Clarifying these rules and focusing resources on building a judicial system that can enforce them and resolve disputes should be a primary goal of any government suffering from corruption ENDEND 
In addition, we know that the more information the public is provided, the easier it will be for your Kenyan brothers and sisters out in the villages to evaluate whether they are being treated fairly by their public servants or not ENDEND  Wealth declarations do little good if no one can access them, and accountability in government spending is not possible if no one knows how much was available and allocated to a given project in the first place ENDEND 
Finally, ethnicbased tribal politics has to stop ENDEND  It is rooted in the bankrupt idea that the goal of politics or business is to funnel as much of the pie as possible to one's family, tribe, or circle with little regard for the public good ENDEND  It stifles innovation and fractures the fabric of the society ENDEND  Instead of opening businesses and engaging in commerce, people come to rely on patronage and payback as a means of advancing ENDEND  Instead of unifying the country to move forward on solving problems, it divides neighbor from neighbor ENDEND 
An accountable, transparent government can break this cycle ENDEND  When people are judged by merit, not connections, then the best and brightest can lead the country, people will work hard, and the entire economy will grow  everyone will benefit and more resources will be available for all, not just select groups ENDEND 
Of course, in the end, one of the strongest weapons your country has against corruption is the ability of you, the people, to stand up and speak out about the injustices you see ENDEND  The Kenyan people are the ultimate guardians against abuses ENDEND 
The world knows the names of Wangari Maathai and John Githongo, who are fighting against the insidious corruption that has weakened Kenya ENDEND  But there are so many others, some of whom I'm meeting during my visit here  Betty Murungi, Ken Njau, Jane Onyango, Maina Kiai, Milly Odhiombo, and Hussein Khalid ENDEND  As well as numerous Kenyan men and women who have refused to pay bribes to get civil servants to perform their duties; the auditors and inspectors general who have done the job before them accurately and fairly, regardless of where the facts have led; the journalists who asked questions and pushed for answers when it may have been more lucrative to look the other way, or whip up a convenient fiction ENDEND  And then there are anonymous Kenyan whistleblowers who show us what is, so that we can all work together to demand what should be ENDEND 
By rejecting the insulting idea that corruption is somehow a part of Kenyan culture, these heroes reveal the very opposite  they reveal a strength and integrity of character that can build a great country, a great future ENDEND  By focusing on building strong, independent institutions  like an anticorruption commission with real authority  rather than cults of personality, they make a contribution to their country that will last longer than their own lives ENDEND  They fight the fight of our time ENDEND 
Looking out at this crowd of young people, I have faith that you will fight this fight too ENDEND 
You will decide if your leaders will be held accountable, or if you will look the other way ENDEND 
You will decide if the standards and the rules will be the same for everyone  regardless of ethnicity or of wealth ENDEND 
And you will determine the direction of this country in the st century  whether the hard work of the many is lost to the selfish desires of a few, or whether you build an open, honest, stronger Kenya where everyone rises together ENDEND 
This is the Kenya that so many who came before you envisioned  all those men and women who struggled and sacrificed and fought for the freedom you enjoy today ENDEND 
I know that honoring their memory and making that freedom real may seem like an impossible task  an effort bigger than you can imagine  but sometimes all it takes to move us there is doing what little you can to right the wrongs you see ENDEND 
As I said at the outset, I did not know my father well  he returned to Kenya from America when I was still young ENDEND  Since that time I have known him through stories  those my mother would tell and those I heard from my relatives here in Kenya on my last trip to this country ENDEND 
I know from these stories that my father was not a perfect man  that he made his share of mistakes and disappointed his share of people in his lifetime ENDEND 
As our parents' children, we have the opportunity to learn from these mistakes and disappointments ENDEND  We have the opportunity to muster the courage to fulfill the promise of our forefathers and lead our great nations towards a better future ENDEND 
In today's Kenya  a Kenya already more open and less repressive than in my father's day  it is that courage that will bring the reform so many of you so desperately want and deserve ENDEND  I wish all of you luck in finding this courage in the days and months to come, and I want you to know that as your ally, your friend, and your brother, I will be there to help in any way I can ENDEND  Thank you ENDEND 

He's absolutely right that Congress has abrogated its oversight responsibilities, and one way to reverse that troubling trend is to adopt a sunset provision in this bill ENDEND  We did that in the Patriot Act, and that allowed us to make important revisions to the bill that reflected our experience about what worked and didn't work during the previous  years ENDEND  We should do that again with this important piece of legislation ENDEND 
But I want to take a few minutes to speak more broadly about the bill before us ENDEND 
I may have only been in this body for a short while, but I am not naive to the political considerations that go along with many of the decisions we make here ENDEND  I realize that soon, we will adjourn for the fall, and the campaigning will begin in earnest ENDEND  And there will be second attack ads and negative mail pieces, and we will be criticized as caring more about the rights of terrorists than the protection of Americans ENDEND  And I know that the vote before us was specifically designed and timed to add more fuel to that fire ENDEND 
And yet, while I know all of this, I'm still disappointed ENDEND  Because what we're doing here today  a debate over the fundamental human rights of the accused  should be bigger than politics ENDEND  This is serious ENDEND 
If this was a debate with obvious ideological differences  heartfelt convictions that couldn't be settled by compromise  I would understand ENDEND  But it's not ENDEND 
All of us  Democrats and Republicans  want to do whatever it takes to track down terrorists and bring them to justice as swiftly as possible ENDEND  All of us want to give our President every tool necessary to do this ENDEND  And all of us were willing to do that in this bill ENDEND  Anyone who says otherwise is lying to the American people ENDEND 
In the five years that the President's system of military tribunals has existed, not one terrorist has been tried ENDEND  Not one has been convicted ENDEND  And in the end, the Supreme Court of the United found the whole thing unconstitutional, which is why we're here today ENDEND 
We could have fixed all of this in a way that allows us to detain and interrogate and try suspected terrorists while still protecting the accidentally accused from spending their lives locked away in Guantanamo Bay ENDEND  Easily ENDEND  This was not an eitheror question ENDEND 
Instead of allowing this President  or any President  to decide what does and does not constitute torture, we could have left the definition up to our own laws and to the Geneva Conventions, as we would have if we passed the bill that the Armed Services committee originally offered ENDEND 
Instead of detainees arriving at Guantanamo and facing a Combatant Status Review Tribunal that allows them no real chance to prove their innocence with evidence or a lawyer, we could have developed a real military system of justice that would sort out the suspected terrorists from the accidentally accused ENDEND 
And instead of not just suspending, but eliminating, the right of habeas corpus  the seven centuryold right of individuals to challenge the terms of their own detention, we could have given the accused one chance  one single chance  to ask the government why they are being held and what they are being charged with ENDEND 
But politics won today ENDEND  Politics won ENDEND  The Administration got its vote, and now it will have its victory lap, and now they will be able to go out on the campaign trail and tell the American people that they were the ones who were tough on the terrorists ENDEND 
And yet, we have a bill that gives the terrorist mastermind of  his day in court, but not the innocent people we may have accidentally rounded up and mistaken for terrorists  people who may stay in prison for the rest of their lives ENDEND 
And yet, we have a report authored by sixteen of our own government's intelligence agencies, a previous draft of which described, and I quote, " ENDEND  ENDEND  ENDEND actions by the United States government that were determined to have stoked the jihad movement, like the indefinite detention of prisoners at Guantanamo Bay ENDEND  ENDEND  ENDEND "
And yet, we have Al Qaeda and the Taliban regrouping in Afghanistan while we look the other way ENDEND  We have a war in Iraq that our own government's intelligence says is serving as Al Qaeda's best recruitment tool ENDEND  And we have recommendations from the bipartisan  commission that we still refuse to implement five years after the fact ENDEND 
The problem with this bill is not that it's too tough on terrorists ENDEND  The problem with this bill is that it's sloppy ENDEND  And the reason it's sloppy is because we rushed it to serve political purposes instead of taking the time to do the job right ENDEND 
I've heard, for example, the argument that it should be military courts, and not federal judges, who should make decisions on these detainees ENDEND  I actually agree with that ENDEND  The problem is that the structure of the military proceedings has been poorly thought through ENDEND  Indeed, the regulations that are supposed to be governing administrative hearings for these detainees, which should have been issued months ago, still haven't been issued ENDEND  Instead, we have rushed through a bill that stands a good chance of being challenged once again in the Supreme Court ENDEND 
This is not how a serious Administration would approach the problem of terrorism ENDEND  I know the President came here today and was insisting that this is supposed to be our primary concern ENDEND  He's absolutely right it should be our primary concern  which is why we should be approaching this with a somberness and seriousness that this Administration has not displayed with this legislation ENDEND 
Now, let me be clear  for those who plot terror against the United States, I hope God has mercy on their soul, because I certainly do not ENDEND  And for those who our government suspects of terror, I support whatever tools are necessary to try them and uncover their plot ENDEND 
But we also know that some have been detained who have no connection to terror whatsoever ENDEND  We've already had reports from the CIA and various generals over the last few years saying that many of the detainees at Guantanamo shouldn't have been there  as one United States   commander of Guantanamo told the Wall Street Journal, "Sometimes, we just didn't get the right folks ENDEND " And we all know about the recent case of the Canadian man who was suspected of terrorist connections, detained in New York, sent to Syria, and tortured, only to find out later that it was all a case of mistaken identity and poor information ENDEND 
In the future, people like this may never have a chance to prove their innocence ENDEND  They may remain locked away forever ENDEND 
And the sad part about all of this is that this betrayal of American values is unnecessary ENDEND  We could've drafted a bipartisan, wellstructured bill that provided adequate due process through the military courts, had an effective review process that would've prevented frivolous lawsuits being filed and kept lawyers from clogging our courts, but upheld the basic ideals that have made this country great ENDEND 
Instead, what we have is a flawed document that in fact betrays the best instincts of some of my colleagues on both sides of the aisle  those who worked in a bipartisan fashion in the Armed Services Committee to craft a bill that we could have been proud of ENDEND  And they essentially got steamrolled by this Administration and by the imperatives of November th ENDEND 
That is not how we should be doing business in the United States   Senate, and that's not how we should be prosecuting this war on terrorism ENDEND  When we're sloppy and cut corners, we are undermining those very virtues of America that will lead us to success in winning this war ENDEND  At bare minimum, I hope we can at least pass this provision so that cooler heads can prevail after the silly season of politics is over ENDEND  Thank you ENDEND Super Tuesday

Before I begin, I just want to send my condolences to the victims of the storms that hit Tennessee and Arkansas ENDEND  They are in our thoughts and in our prayers ENDEND 
Well, the polls are just closing in California and the votes are still being counted in cities and towns across the country ENDEND  But there is one thing on this February night that we do not need the final results to know  our time has come, our movement is real, and change is coming to America ENDEND 
Only a few hundred miles from here, almost one year ago to the day, we stood on the steps of the Old State Capitol to reaffirm a truth that was spoken there so many generations ago  that a house divided cannot stand; that we are more than a collection of Red States and Blue States; we are, and always will be, the United States of America ENDEND 
What began as a whisper in Springfield soon carried across the corn fields of Iowa, where farmers and factory workers; students and seniors stood up in numbers we've never seen ENDEND  They stood up to say that maybe this year, we don't have to settle for a politics where scoring points is more important than solving problems ENDEND  This time we can finally do something about health care we can't afford or mortgages we can't pay ENDEND  This time can be different ENDEND 
Their voices echoed from the hills of New Hampshire to the deserts of Nevada, where teachers and cooks and kitchen workers stood up to say that maybe Washington doesn't have to be run by lobbyists anymore ENDEND  They reached the coast of South Carolina when people said that maybe we don't have to be divided by race and region and gender; that crumbling schools are stealing the future of black children and white children; that we can come together and build an America that gives every child, everywhere the opportunity to live their dreams ENDEND  This time can be different ENDEND 
And today, on this Tuesday in February, in states North and South, East and West, what began as a whisper in Springfield has swelled to a chorus of millions calling for change ENDEND  A chorus that cannot be ignored ENDEND  That cannot be deterred ENDEND  This time can be different because this campaign for the presidency is different ENDEND 
It's different not because of me, but because of you ENDEND  Because you are tired of being disappointed and tired of being let down ENDEND  You're tired of hearing promises made and plans proposed in the heat of a campaign only to have nothing change when everyone goes back to Washington ENDEND  Because the lobbyists just write another check ENDEND  Or because politicians start worrying about how they'll win the next election instead of why they should ENDEND  Or because they focus on who's up and who's down instead of who matters ENDEND 
And while Washington is consumed with the same drama and division and distraction, another family puts up a For Sale sign in the front yard ENDEND  Another factory shuts its doors ENDEND  Another soldier waves goodbye as he leaves on another tour of duty in a war that should've never been authorized and never been waged ENDEND  It goes on and on and on ENDEND 
But in this election  at this moment  you are standing up all across this country to say, not this time ENDEND  Not this year ENDEND  The stakes are too high and the challenges too great to play the same Washington game with the same Washington players and expect a different result ENDEND  This time must be different ENDEND 
Now, this isn't about me and it's not about Senator Clinton ENDEND  As I've said before, she was a friend before this campaign and she'll be a friend after it's over ENDEND  I respect her as a colleague, and I congratulate her on her victories tonight ENDEND

It's a choice between having a debate with the other party about who has the most experience in Washington, or having one about who's most likely to change Washington ENDEND  Because that's a debate we can win ENDEND 
It's a choice between a candidate who's taken more money from Washington lobbyists than either Republican in this race, and a campaign that hasn't taken a dime of their money because we've been funded by you ENDEND 
And if I am your nominee, my opponent will not be able to say that I voted for the war in Iraq; or that I gave George Bush the benefit of the doubt on Iran; or that I support the BushCheney policy of not talking to leaders we don't like ENDEND  And he will not be able to say that I wavered on something as fundamental as whether or not it's ok for America to use torture  because it is never ok ENDEND  That is the choice in this election ENDEND 
The Republicans running for President have already tied themselves to the past ENDEND  They speak of a hundred year war in Iraq and billions more on tax breaks for the wealthiest few who don't need them and didn't ask for them  tax breaks that mortgage our children's future on a mountain of debt at a time when there are families who can't pay their medical bills and students who can't pay their tuition ENDEND

And when I am President, we will put an end to a politics that uses  as a way to scare up votes, and start seeing it as a challenge that should unite America and the world against the common threats of the twentyfirst century: terrorism and nuclear weapons; climate change and poverty; genocide and disease ENDEND 
We can do this ENDEND  It will not be easy ENDEND  It will require struggle and sacrifice ENDEND  There will setbacks and we will make mistakes ENDEND  And that is why we need all the help we can get ENDEND  So tonight I want to speak directly to all those Americans who have yet to join this movement but still hunger for change  we need you ENDEND  We need you to stand with us, and work with us, and help us prove that together, ordinary people can still do extraordinary things ENDEND 
I am blessed to be standing in the city where my own extraordinary journey began ENDEND  A few miles from here, in the shadow of a shuttered steel plant, is where I learned what it takes to make change happen ENDEND 
I was a young organizer then, intent on fighting joblessness and poverty on the South Side, and I still remember one of the very first meetings I put together ENDEND  We had worked on it for days, but no one showed up ENDEND  Our volunteers felt so defeated, they wanted to quit ENDEND  And to be honest, so did I ENDEND

Good morning ENDEND  I appreciate the opportunity to speak here at the Call to Renewal's Building a Covenant for a New America conference ENDEND  I've had the opportunity to take a look at your Covenant for a New America ENDEND  It is filled with outstanding policies and prescriptions for much of what ails this country ENDEND  So I'd like to congratulate you all on the thoughtful presentations you've given so far about poverty and justice in America, and for putting fire under the feet of the political leadership here in Washington ENDEND 
But today I'd like to talk about the connection between religion and politics and perhaps offer some thoughts about how we can sort through some of the often bitter arguments that we've been seeing over the last several years ENDEND 
I do so because, as you all know, we can affirm the importance of poverty in the Bible; and we can raise up and pass out this Covenant for a New America ENDEND  We can talk to the press, and we can discuss the religious call to address poverty and environmental stewardship all we want, but it won't have an impact unless we tackle headon the mutual suspicion that sometimes exists between religious America and secular America ENDEND 
I want to give you an example that I think illustrates this fact ENDEND  As some of you know, during the  United States   Senate General Election I ran against a gentleman named Alan Keyes ENDEND  Mr. Keyes is wellversed in the Jerry FalwellPat Robertson style of rhetoric that often labels progressives as both immoral and godless ENDEND 
Indeed, Mr. Keyes announced towards the end of the campaign that, "Jesus Christ would not vote for Barack Obama ENDEND  Christ would not vote for Barack Obama because Barack Obama has behaved in a way that it is inconceivable for Christ to have behaved ENDEND "
Jesus Christ would not vote for Barack Obama ENDEND 
Now, I was urged by some of my liberal supporters not to take this statement seriously, to essentially ignore it ENDEND  To them, Mr. Keyes was an extremist, and his arguments not worth entertaining ENDEND  And since at the time, I was up  points in the polls, it probably wasn't a bad piece of strategic advice ENDEND 
But what they didn't understand, however, was that I had to take Mr. Keyes seriously, for he claimed to speak for my religion, and my God ENDEND  He claimed knowledge of certain truths ENDEND 
Mr. Obama says he's a Christian, he was saying, and yet he supports a lifestyle that the Bible calls an abomination ENDEND 
Mr. Obama says he's a Christian, but supports the destruction of innocent and sacred life ENDEND 
And so what would my supporters have me say? How should I respond? Should I say that a literalist reading of the Bible was folly? Should I say that Mr. Keyes, who is a Roman Catholic, should ignore the teachings of the Pope?
Unwilling to go there, I answered with what has come to be the typically liberal response in such debates  namely, I said that we live in a pluralistic society, that I can't impose my own religious views on another, that I was running to be the United States   Senator of Illinois and not the Minister of Illinois ENDEND 
But Mr. Keyes's implicit accusation that I was not a true Christian nagged at me, and I was also aware that my answer did not adequately address the role my faith has in guiding my own values and my own beliefs ENDEND 
Now, my dilemma was by no means unique ENDEND  In a way, it reflected the broader debate we've been having in this country for the last thirty years over the role of religion in politics ENDEND 
For some time now, there has been plenty of talk among pundits and pollsters that the political divide in this country has fallen sharply along religious lines ENDEND  Indeed, the single biggest "gap" in party affiliation among white Americans today is not between men and women, or those who reside in socalled Red States and those who reside in Blue, but between those who attend church regularly and those who don't ENDEND 
Conservative leaders have been all too happy to exploit this gap, consistently reminding evangelical Christians that Democrats disrespect their values and dislike their Church, while suggesting to the rest of the country that religious Americans care only about issues like abortion and gay marriage; school prayer and intelligent design ENDEND 
Democrats, for the most part, have taken the bait ENDEND  At best, we may try to avoid the conversation about religious values altogether, fearful of offending anyone and claiming that  regardless of our personal beliefs  constitutional principles tie our hands ENDEND  At worst, there are some liberals who dismiss religion in the public square as inherently irrational or intolerant, insisting on a caricature of religious Americans that paints them as fanatical, or thinking that the very word "Christian" describes one's political opponents, not people of faith ENDEND 
Now, such strategies of avoidance may work for progressives when our opponent is Alan Keyes ENDEND  But over the long haul, I think we make a mistake when we fail to acknowledge the power of faith in people's lives  in the lives of the American people  and I think it's time that we join a serious debate about how to reconcile faith with our modern, pluralistic democracy ENDEND 
And if we're going to do that then we first need to understand that Americans are a religious people ENDEND   percent of us believe in God,  percent affiliate themselves with an organized religion,  percent call themselves committed Christians, and substantially more people in America believe in angels than they do in evolution ENDEND 
This religious tendency is not simply the result of successful marketing by skilled preachers or the draw of popular megachurches ENDEND  In fact, it speaks to a hunger that's deeper than that  a hunger that goes beyond any particular issue or cause ENDEND 
Each day, it seems, thousands of Americans are going about their daily rounds  dropping off the kids at school, driving to the office, flying to a business meeting, shopping at the mall, trying to stay on their diets  and they're coming to the realization that something is missing ENDEND  They are deciding that their work, their possessions, their diversions, their sheer busyness, is not enough ENDEND 
They want a sense of purpose, a narrative arc to their lives ENDEND  They're looking to relieve a chronic loneliness, a feeling supported by a recent study that shows Americans have fewer close friends and confidants than ever before ENDEND  And so they need an assurance that somebody out there cares about them, is listening to them  that they are not just destined to travel down that long highway towards nothingness ENDEND 
And I speak with some experience on this matter ENDEND  I was not raised in a particularly religious household, as undoubtedly many in the audience were ENDEND  My father, who returned to Kenya when I was just two, was born Muslim but as an adult became an atheist ENDEND  My mother, whose parents were nonpracticing Baptists and Methodists, was probably one of the most spiritual and kindest people I've ever known, but grew up with a healthy skepticism of organized religion herself ENDEND  As a consequence, so did I ENDEND 
It wasn't until after college, when I went to Chicago to work as a community organizer for a group of Christian churches, that I confronted my own spiritual dilemma ENDEND 
I was working with churches, and the Christians who I worked with recognized themselves in me ENDEND  They saw that I knew their Book and that I shared their values and sang their songs ENDEND  But they sensed that a part of me that remained removed, detached, that I was an observer in their midst ENDEND 
And in time, I came to realize that something was missing as well  that without a vessel for my beliefs, without a commitment to a particular community of faith, at some level I would always remain apart, and alone ENDEND 
And if it weren't for the particular attributes of the historically black church, I may have accepted this fate ENDEND  But as the months passed in Chicago, I found myself drawn  not just to work with the church, but to be in the church ENDEND 
For one thing, I believed and still believe in the power of the AfricanAmerican religious tradition to spur social change, a power made real by some of the leaders here today ENDEND  Because of its past, the black church understands in an intimate way the Biblical call to feed the hungry and cloth the naked and challenge powers and principalities ENDEND  And in its historical struggles for freedom and the rights of man, I was able to see faith as more than just a comfort to the weary or a hedge against death, but rather as an active, palpable agent in the world ENDEND  As a source of hope ENDEND 
And perhaps it was out of this intimate knowledge of hardship  the grounding of faith in struggle  that the church offered me a second insight, one that I think is important to emphasize today ENDEND 
Faith doesn't mean that you don't have doubts ENDEND 
You need to come to church in the first place precisely because you are first of this world, not apart from it ENDEND  You need to embrace Christ precisely because you have sins to wash away  because you are human and need an ally in this difficult journey ENDEND 
It was because of these newfound understandings that I was finally able to walk down the aisle of Trinity United Church of Christ on th Street in the Southside of Chicago one day and affirm my Christian faith ENDEND  It came about as a choice, and not an epiphany ENDEND  I didn't fall out in church ENDEND  The questions I had didn't magically disappear ENDEND  But kneeling beneath that cross on the South Side, I felt that I heard God's spirit beckoning me ENDEND  I submitted myself to His will, and dedicated myself to discovering His truth ENDEND 
That's a path that has been shared by millions upon millions of Americans  evangelicals, Catholics, Protestants, Jews and Muslims alike; some since birth, others at certain turning points in their lives ENDEND  It is not something they set apart from the rest of their beliefs and values ENDEND  In fact, it is often what drives their beliefs and their values ENDEND 
And that is why that, if we truly hope to speak to people where they're at  to communicate our hopes and values in a way that's relevant to their own  then as progressives, we cannot abandon the field of religious discourse ENDEND 
Because when we ignore the debate about what it means to be a good Christian or Muslim or Jew; when we discuss religion only in the negative sense of where or how it should not be practiced, rather than in the positive sense of what it tells us about our obligations towards one another; when we shy away from religious venues and religious broadcasts because we assume that we will be unwelcome  others will fill the vacuum, those with the most insular views of faith, or those who cynically use religion to justify partisan ends ENDEND 
In other words, if we don't reach out to evangelical Christians and other religious Americans and tell them what we stand for, then the Jerry Falwells and Pat Robertsons and Alan Keyeses will continue to hold sway ENDEND 
More fundamentally, the discomfort of some progressives with any hint of religion has often prevented us from effectively addressing issues in moral terms ENDEND  Some of the problem here is rhetorical  if we scrub language of all religious content, we forfeit the imagery and terminology through which millions of Americans understand both their personal morality and social justice ENDEND 
Imagine Lincoln's Second Inaugural Address without reference to "the judgments of the Lord ENDEND " Or King's I Have a Dream speech without references to "all of God's children ENDEND " Their summoning of a higher truth helped inspire what had seemed impossible, and move the nation to embrace a common destiny ENDEND 
Our failure as progressives to tap into the moral underpinnings of the nation is not just rhetorical, though ENDEND  Our fear of getting "preachy" may also lead us to discount the role that values and culture play in some of our most urgent social problems ENDEND 
After all, the problems of poverty and racism, the uninsured and the unemployed, are not simply technical problems in search of the perfect ten point plan ENDEND  They are rooted in both societal indifference and individual callousness  in the imperfections of man ENDEND 
Solving these problems will require changes in government policy, but it will also require changes in hearts and a change in minds ENDEND  I believe in keeping guns out of our inner cities, and that our leaders must say so in the face of the gun manufacturers' lobby  but I also believe that when a gangbanger shoots indiscriminately into a crowd because he feels somebody disrespected him, we've got a moral problem ENDEND  There's a hole in that young man's heart  a hole that the government alone cannot fix ENDEND 
I believe in vigorous enforcement of our nondiscrimination laws ENDEND  But I also believe that a transformation of conscience and a genuine commitment to diversity on the part of the nation's CEOs could bring about quicker results than a battalion of lawyers ENDEND  They have more lawyers than us anyway ENDEND 
I think that we should put more of our tax dollars into educating poor girls and boys ENDEND  I think that the work that Marian Wright Edelman has done all her life is absolutely how we should prioritize our resources in the wealthiest nation on earth ENDEND  I also think that we should give them the information about contraception that can prevent unwanted pregnancies, lower abortion rates, and help assure that that every child is loved and cherished ENDEND 
But, you know, my Bible tells me that if we train a child in the way he should go, when he is old he will not turn from it ENDEND  So I think faith and guidance can help fortify a young woman's sense of self, a young man's sense of responsibility, and a sense of reverence that all young people should have for the act of sexual intimacy ENDEND 
I am not suggesting that every progressive suddenly latch on to religious terminology  that can be dangerous ENDEND  Nothing is more transparent than inauthentic expressions of faith ENDEND  As Jim has mentioned, some politicians come and clap  off rhythm  to the choir ENDEND  We don't need that ENDEND 
In fact, because I do not believe that religious people have a monopoly on morality, I would rather have someone who is grounded in morality and ethics, and who is also secular, affirm their morality and ethics and values without pretending that they're something they're not ENDEND  They don't need to do that ENDEND  None of us need to do that ENDEND 
But what I am suggesting is this  secularists are wrong when they ask believers to leave their religion at the door before entering into the public square ENDEND  Frederick Douglas, Abraham Lincoln, Williams Jennings Bryant, Dorothy Day, Martin Luther King  indeed, the majority of great reformers in American history  were not only motivated by faith, but repeatedly used religious language to argue for their cause ENDEND  So to say that men and women should not inject their "personal morality" into public policy debates is a practical absurdity ENDEND  Our law is by definition a codification of morality, much of it grounded in the JudeoChristian tradition ENDEND 
Moreover, if we progressives shed some of these biases, we might recognize some overlapping values that both religious and secular people share when it comes to the moral and material direction of our country ENDEND  We might recognize that the call to sacrifice on behalf of the next generation, the need to think in terms of "thou" and not just "I," resonates in religious congregations all across the country ENDEND  And we might realize that we have the ability to reach out to the evangelical community and engage millions of religious Americans in the larger project of American renewal ENDEND 
Some of this is already beginning to happen ENDEND  Pastors, friends of mine like Rick Warren and T ENDEND D ENDEND  Jakes are wielding their enormous influences to confront AIDS, Third World debt relief, and the genocide in Darfur ENDEND  Religious thinkers and activists like our good friend Jim Wallis and Tony Campolo are lifting up the Biblical injunction to help the poor as a means of mobilizing Christians against budget cuts to social programs and growing inequality ENDEND 
And by the way, we need Christians on Capitol Hill, Jews on Capitol Hill and Muslims on Capitol Hill talking about the estate tax ENDEND  When you've got an estate tax debate that proposes a trillion dollars being taken out of social programs to go to a handful of folks who don't need and weren't even asking for it, you know that we need an injection of morality in our political debate ENDEND 
Across the country, individual churches like my own and your own are sponsoring day care programs, building senior centers, helping exoffenders reclaim their lives, and rebuilding our gulf coast in the aftermath of Hurricane Katrina ENDEND 
So the question is, how do we build on these stilltentative partnerships between religious and secular people of good will? It's going to take more work, a lot more work than we've done so far ENDEND  The tensions and the suspicions on each side of the religious divide will have to be squarely addressed ENDEND  And each side will need to accept some ground rules for collaboration ENDEND 
While I've already laid out some of the work that progressive leaders need to do, I want to talk a little bit about what conservative leaders need to do  some truths they need to acknowledge ENDEND 
For one, they need to understand the critical role that the separation of church and state has played in preserving not only our democracy, but the robustness of our religious practice ENDEND  Folks tend to forget that during our founding, it wasn't the atheists or the civil libertarians who were the most effective champions of the First Amendment ENDEND  It was the persecuted minorities, it was Baptists like John Leland who didn't want the established churches to impose their views on folks who were getting happy out in the fields and teaching the scripture to slaves ENDEND  It was the forbearers of the evangelicals who were the most adamant about not mingling government with religious, because they did not want statesponsored religion hindering their ability to practice their faith as they understood it ENDEND 
Moreover, given the increasing diversity of America's population, the dangers of sectarianism have never been greater ENDEND  Whatever we once were, we are no longer just a Christian nation; we are also a Jewish nation, a Muslim nation, a Buddhist nation, a Hindu nation, and a nation of nonbelievers ENDEND 
And even if we did have only Christians in our midst, if we expelled every nonChristian from the United States of America, whose Christianity would we teach in the schools? Would we go with James Dobson's, or Al Sharpton's? Which passages of Scripture should guide our public policy? Should we go with Leviticus, which suggests slavery is ok and that eating shellfish is abomination? How about Deuteronomy, which suggests stoning your child if he strays from the faith? Or should we just stick to the Sermon on the Mount  a passage that is so radical that it's doubtful that our own Defense Department would survive its application? So before we get carried away, let's read our bibles ENDEND  Folks haven't been reading their bibles ENDEND 
This brings me to my second point ENDEND  Democracy demands that the religiously motivated translate their concerns into universal, rather than religionspecific, values ENDEND  It requires that their proposals be subject to argument, and amenable to reason ENDEND  I may be opposed to abortion for religious reasons, but if I seek to pass a law banning the practice, I cannot simply point to the teachings of my church or evoke God's will ENDEND  I have to explain why abortion violates some principle that is accessible to people of all faiths, including those with no faith at all ENDEND 
Now this is going to be difficult for some who believe in the inerrancy of the Bible, as many evangelicals do ENDEND  But in a pluralistic democracy, we have no choice ENDEND  Politics depends on our ability to persuade each other of common aims based on a common reality ENDEND  It involves the compromise, the art of what's possible ENDEND  At some fundamental level, religion does not allow for compromise ENDEND  It's the art of the impossible ENDEND  If God has spoken, then followers are expected to live up to God's edicts, regardless of the consequences ENDEND  To base one's life on such uncompromising commitments may be sublime, but to base our policy making on such commitments would be a dangerous thing ENDEND  And if you doubt that, let me give you an example ENDEND 
We all know the story of Abraham and Isaac ENDEND  Abraham is ordered by God to offer up his only son, and without argument, he takes Isaac to the mountaintop, binds him to an altar, and raises his knife, prepared to act as God has commanded ENDEND 
Of course, in the end God sends down an angel to intercede at the very last minute, and Abraham passes God's test of devotion ENDEND 
But it's fair to say that if any of us leaving this church saw Abraham on a roof of a building raising his knife, we would, at the very least, call the police and expect the Department of Children and Family Services to take Isaac away from Abraham ENDEND  We would do so because we do not hear what Abraham hears, do not see what Abraham sees, true as those experiences may be ENDEND  So the best we can do is act in accordance with those things that we all see, and that we all hear, be it common laws or basic reason ENDEND 
Finally, any reconciliation between faith and democratic pluralism requires some sense of proportion ENDEND 
This goes for both sides ENDEND 
Even those who claim the Bible's inerrancy make distinctions between Scriptural edicts, sensing that some passages  the Ten Commandments, say, or a belief in Christ's divinity  are central to Christian faith, while others are more culturally specific and may be modified to accommodate modern life ENDEND 
The American people intuitively understand this, which is why the majority of Catholics practice birth control and some of those opposed to gay marriage nevertheless are opposed to a Constitutional amendment to ban it ENDEND  Religious leadership need not accept such wisdom in counseling their flocks, but they should recognize this wisdom in their politics ENDEND 
But a sense of proportion should also guide those who police the boundaries between church and state ENDEND  Not every mention of God in public is a breach to the wall of separation  context matters ENDEND  It is doubtful that children reciting the Pledge of Allegiance feel oppressed or brainwashed as a consequence of muttering the phrase "under God ENDEND " I didn't ENDEND  Having voluntary student prayer groups use school property to meet should not be a threat, any more than its use by the High School Republicans should threaten Democrats ENDEND  And one can envision certain faithbased programs  targeting exoffenders or substance abusers  that offer a uniquely powerful way of solving problems ENDEND 
So we all have some work to do here ENDEND  But I am hopeful that we can bridge the gaps that exist and overcome the prejudices each of us bring to this debate ENDEND  And I have faith that millions of believing Americans want that to happen ENDEND  No matter how religious they may or may not be, people are tired of seeing faith used as a tool of attack ENDEND  They don't want faith used to belittle or to divide ENDEND  They're tired of hearing folks deliver more screed than sermon ENDEND  Because in the end, that's not how they think about faith in their own lives ENDEND 
So let me end with just one other interaction I had during my campaign ENDEND  A few days after I won the Democratic nomination in my United States   Senate race, I received an email from a doctor at the University of Chicago Medical School that said the following:
"Congratulations on your overwhelming and inspiring primary win ENDEND  I was happy to vote for you, and I will tell you that I am seriously considering voting for you in the general election ENDEND  I write to express my concerns that may, in the end, prevent me from supporting you ENDEND "
The doctor described himself as a Christian who understood his commitments to be "totalizing ENDEND " His faith led him to a strong opposition to abortion and gay marriage, although he said that his faith also led him to question the idolatry of the free market and quick resort to militarism that seemed to characterize much of the Republican agenda ENDEND 
But the reason the doctor was considering not voting for me was not simply my position on abortion ENDEND  Rather, he had read an entry that my campaign had posted on my website, which suggested that I would fight "rightwing ideologues who want to take away a woman's right to choose ENDEND " The doctor went on to write:
"I sense that you have a strong sense of justice ENDEND  ENDEND  ENDEND and I also sense that you are a fair minded person with a high regard for reason ENDEND  ENDEND  ENDEND Whatever your convictions, if you truly believe that those who oppose abortion are all ideologues driven by perverse desires to inflict suffering on women, then you, in my judgment, are not fairminded ENDEND  ENDEND  ENDEND  ENDEND You know that we enter times that are fraught with possibilities for good and for harm, times when we are struggling to make sense of a common polity in the context of plurality, when we are unsure of what grounds we have for making any claims that involve others ENDEND  ENDEND  ENDEND I do not ask at this point that you oppose abortion, only that you speak about this issue in fairminded words ENDEND "
Fairminded words ENDEND 
So I looked at my website and found the offending words ENDEND  In fairness to them, my staff had written them using standard Democratic boilerplate language to summarize my prochoice position during the Democratic primary, at a time when some of my opponents were questioning my commitment to protect Roe v ENDEND  Wade ENDEND 
Rereading the doctor's letter, though, I felt a pang of shame ENDEND  It is people like him who are looking for a deeper, fuller conversation about religion in this country ENDEND  They may not change their positions, but they are willing to listen and learn from those who are willing to speak in fairminded words ENDEND  Those who know of the central and awesome place that God holds in the lives of so many, and who refuse to treat faith as simply another political issue with which to score points ENDEND 
So I wrote back to the doctor, and I thanked him for his advice ENDEND  The next day, I circulated the email to my staff and changed the language on my website to state in clear but simple terms my prochoice position ENDEND  And that night, before I went to bed, I said a prayer of my own  a prayer that I might extend the same presumption of good faith to others that the doctor had extended to me ENDEND 
And that night, before I went to bed I said a prayer of my own ENDEND  It's a prayer I think I share with a lot of Americans ENDEND  A hope that we can live with one another in a way that reconciles the beliefs of each with the good of all ENDEND  It's a prayer worth praying, and a conversation worth having in this country in the months and years to come ENDEND  Thank you ENDEND

The topic today is net neutrality ENDEND  The internet today is an open platform where the demand for websites and services dictates success ENDEND  You've got barriers to entry that are low and equal for all comers ENDEND  And it's because the internet is a neutral platform that I can put on this podcast and transmit it over the internet without having to go through some corporate media middleman ENDEND  I can say what I want without censorship ENDEND  I don't have to pay a special charge ENDEND  But the big telephone and cable companies want to change the internet as we know it ENDEND  They say they want to create highspeed lanes on the internet and strike exclusive contractual arrangements with internet contentproviders for access to those highspeed lanes ENDEND  Those of us who can't pony up the cash for these highspeed connections will be relegated to the slow lanes ENDEND 
Allowing the Bells and cable companies to act as gatekeepers with control over internet access would make the internet like cable ENDEND  A producerdriven market with barriers to entry for website creators and preferential treatment for specific sites based not on merit, the number of hits, but on relationships with the corporate gatekeeper ENDEND  If there were four or more competitive providers of broadband service to every home, then cable and telephone companies would not be able to create a bidding war for access to the highspeed lanes ENDEND  But here's the problem ENDEND  More than  percent of households get their broadband services from either cable or a telephone company ENDEND 
So here's my view ENDEND  We can't have a situation in which the corporate duopoly dictates the future of the internet and that's why I'm supporting what is called net neutrality ENDEND  In the House, the Energy and Commerce Committee and the Judiciary Committee reached different conclusions on network neutrality ENDEND  Judiciary Committee members voted to protect net neutrality and commerce voted with the Bells and cable ENDEND  That debate is going to hit the House floor this Friday ENDEND  In the Senate, Senators Snowe and Dorgan are leading the fight for net neutrality and I've joined in that effort ENDEND  Senator Inouye, the ranking Democrat of the Commerce Committee, has joined us in this effort as well and he's working with Senator Stevens to put strong network neutrality into any Senate bill that comes before us ENDEND  There is widespread support among consumer groups, leading academics and the most innovative internet companies, including Google and Yahoo, in favor of net neutrality ENDEND  And part of the reason for that is companies like Google and Yahoo might never have gotten started had they not been in a position to easily access the internet and do so on the same terms as the big corporate companies that were interested in making money on the internet ENDEND 
I know if you are listening to this podcast that you are going to take an intense interest in this issue as well ENDEND  Congress is going to need to hear your voice because the Bell and cable companies are going to be dedicating millions of dollars to defeating network neutrality ENDEND  So I'll keep you updated on this important issue and I look forward to talking to you guys again next week ENDEND  

I come to the floor today to discuss the bipartisan employment verification system amendment that Senators Grassley, Kennedy, Kyl, and I have introduced ENDEND 
One of the central components of immigration reform is enforcement, and this bill contains a number of important provisions to beef up border security ENDEND  But that's not enough ENDEND  Real enforcement also means drying up the pool of jobs that encourages illegal immigration ENDEND  And that can only happen if employers don't hire illegal workers ENDEND  Unfortunately, our current employer enforcement system does little to nothing to deter illegal immigrants from finding work ENDEND 
Overall, the number of workplace arrests of illegal immigrants fell from , in  to  in , even as illegal immigration grew during that time ENDEND  Moreover, between  to  of all undocumented immigrants are people who have overstayed their visas ENDEND  And the only way to effectively deter overstays is to reduce access to employment ENDEND 
When Congress last passed an immigration bill in , we didn't provide a meaningful way for employers to check legal eligibility to work ENDEND  Currently, employees can prove their legal status by showing a variety of documents, and employers are supposed to record their inspection of such documents by filling out an I form for each employee ENDEND  As a result, the market for fraudulent documents  fake Social Security cards, driver's licenses, birth certificates  has exploded ENDEND 
But, with more than  million employees in more than  million workplaces, and only about  Wage and Hour investigators, employer sanctions have become merely a nuisance requirement to maintain records, not a serious risk of penalties ENDEND  As a result, the number of "intent to fine" notices issued to employers for hiring undocumented workers dropped from  in  to just three in  ENDEND 
Understandably, employers cannot always detect forged documents ENDEND  And employers who reject workers with questionable documents risk an employment discrimination suit ENDEND 
That's why we need a better alternative ENDEND  We need an electronic verification system that can effectively detect the use of fraudulent documents, significantly reduce the employment of illegal workers, and give employers the confidence that their workforce is legal ENDEND 
When Congress first considered comprehensive immigration reform in April, the legislation on the floor addressed this problem by creating a national employment eligibility verification system ENDEND  Senators Grassley, Kyl, and I all thought that was a good idea in theory, but we had concerns with the design of the system ENDEND 
Senators Grassley and Kyl proposed that the verification system be implemented nationally within  months ENDEND 
Senators Kennedy and I proposed that the system be phased in over five years but that it also include additional accuracy and privacy standards, as well as strict prohibitions on use of the system to discriminate against workers ENDEND 
For the past few weeks, our staffs have worked together in a bipartisan effort to negotiate a substitute that took the concerns of both proposals into consideration ENDEND  I'm pleased that we've reached an agreement ENDEND 
Under our compromise amendment, all employers would have to participate  months after the Department of Homeland Security receives the appropriations needed to fund the system ENDEND  All new employees hired would have to be run through the system, and a series of privacy and accuracy standards would protect citizens and legal immigrants from errors in the system and breaches of private information ENDEND 
And to make sure that employers take the system seriously, we strengthen civil penalties for employers who hire unauthorized workers, and we establish criminal penalties for repeat violators ENDEND 
We've worked in a constructive, bipartisan manner to design an employment verification system that is fair to legal workers and tough on illegal workers ENDEND  This is a good amendment, and I urge my colleagues to support it ENDEND 

Today, we take up the valuable time of the United States   Senate with a proposed amendment to our Constitution that has absolutely no chance of passing ENDEND 
We do this, allegedly, in an attempt to uphold the institution of marriage in this country ENDEND  We do this despite the fact that for over two hundred years, Americans have been defining and defending marriage on the state and local level without any help from the United States   Constitution at all ENDEND 
And yet, we're here anyway because it's an election year  because the party in power has decided that the best way to get voters to the polls is not by talking about Iraq or health care or energy or education, but about a constitutional ban on samesex marriage that they have no chance of passing ENDEND 
Now, I realize that for some Americans, this is an important issue ENDEND  And I should say that personally, I do believe that marriage is between a man and a woman ENDEND 
But let's be honest ENDEND  That's not what this debate is about ENDEND  Not at this time ENDEND 
This debate is an attempt to break a consensus that is quietly being forged in this country ENDEND  It's a consensus between Democrats and Republicans, liberals and conservatives, Red States and Blue States, that it's time for new leadership in this country  leadership that will stop dividing us, stop disappointing us, and start addressing the problems facing most Americans ENDEND 
It's a consensus between a majority of Americans who say, "You know what, maybe some of us are comfortable with gay marriage right now and some of us are not ENDEND  But most of us do believe that gay couples should be able to visit each other in the hospital and share health care benefits; most of us do believe that they should be treated with dignity and have their privacy respected by the federal government ENDEND "
And we all know that if this amendment were to pass, it would close the door on much of this  because we know that when similar amendments passed in places like Ohio and Michigan and Utah, domestic partnership benefits were taken away from gay couples ENDEND 
This is not what the majority of the American people want ENDEND  And this is not about trying to build consensus in this country; it's not about trying to bring people together ENDEND 
This is about winning an election ENDEND  That's why the issue was last raised in July of , and that's why we haven't heard about it again until now ENDEND  And while this is supposedly a measure that the other party raised to appeal to some of its core supporters, I don't know how happy I'd be if my party only talked about an issue I cared about right around election time  especially if they knew it had no chance of passing ENDEND 
I agree with most Americans, with Democrats and Republicans, with Vice President Cheney, with over , religious leaders of all different beliefs, that decisions about marriage, as they always have, should be left to the states ENDEND 
Today, we should take this amendment only for what it is  a political ploy designed to rally a few supporters and draw the country's attention away from this leadership's past failures and America's future challenges ENDEND 
There is plenty of work to be done in this country ENDEND  There are millions without health care and skyrocketing gas prices and children in crumbling schools and thousands of young Americans risking their lives in Iraq ENDEND 
So don't tell me that this is the best use of our time ENDEND  Don't tell me that this is what people want to see talked about on TV and in the newspapers all day ENDEND  We wonder why the American people have such a low opinion of Washington these days ENDEND  This is why ENDEND 
We are better than this ENDEND  And we certainly owe the American people more than this ENDEND  I know that this amendment will fail, and when it does, I hope we can start discussing issues and offering proposals that will actually improve the lives of most Americans ENDEND 

For more than two years now, we have been watching a rolling genocide take place in Darfur, western Sudan ENDEND  Many of you I'm sure are aware of the tragedy that has been unfolding there ENDEND  For those of you who are not, essentially what we have seen is a systematic targeting on the part of the Khartoum government and the Janjaweed Arab militia that have systematically uprooted, killed, murdered, pillaged, raped, Africans, driven them from their homes into enormous displacedperson camps ENDEND  Refugee camps, within Sudan ENDEND  It's estimated that at least , people have been killed ENDEND  It's known that at least  million people have been displaced ENDEND  The administration early on in this tragedy acknowledged that this was genocide that was taking place ENDEND  I think there has been broad recognition in the international community that the behavior of the Sudanese government has been scandalous ENDEND  The rationale that has provided from the Sudanese government for what has been taking place is that there is a battle going on between Sudanese government and rebels that operate within the area ENDEND  But, the real victims have not been rebel sympathizers, or the rebels themselves, they've been innocent men, women and children ENDEND 
For more than a year now, I've been working with other Senators to see what we can do to really push the Administration to take this as seriously as it warrants ENDEND  To the Administration's credit, the United States government has probably paid more attention to this issue than some of our European allies ENDEND  We have been a major contributor of aid to the region; we have helped to finance the African Union, to provide peacekeeping forces in the Darfur area ENDEND  So, in a lot of ways, the United States government has been much more on top of this than Europeans, Canadians, and others, who oftentimes accuse the Untied States of being indifferent to the problems of the third world ENDEND  On the other hand, what has been done is not enough ENDEND  The few thousand African Union troops who have been placed in Darfur are primarily providing witness to some of the atrocities that are taking place there, but they don't have clear rules of engagement, they are underarmed, undertrained, they don't really provide the sort of protective force that would be needed to not only ensure that existing villages aren't ravaged by the Janjaweeds, but more importantly, that the  million displaced people could actually safely start returning home ENDEND 
Recent reports indicate that in the past few weeks alone, more than , people have been displaced ENDEND  There are also indications that the Janjaweed, recognizing that the AU forces, the African Union forces, are not particularly effective, have started targeting them ENDEND  So there is a sense of deterioration in Darfur, the situation may be getting worse, rather than better ENDEND  And, what's most disturbing is that the United States government seems to be backing off a little bit, the commitment that it made to deal with the problem ENDEND  There was a quote from the undersecretary for African Affairs, Secretary Frasier, in which she indicated that, maybe this was not a genocide after all ENDEND  And, if that ends up being the United State's attitude, then we could see continuing problems of a scale that might eventually reach the same scale in which happened in Rwanda ENDEND 
So, here are a couple of things that we think need to happen ENDEND  Number one: we need a UN peacekeeping mission in Darfur ENDEND  There have been conversations; the UN Secretary General, Koffee Annan, the AU forces, and the Bush Administration have all acknowledged this ENDEND  There's got to be a sense of urgency in which the US diplomatic efforts are focused on getting this UN peacekeeping force up to about , troops, and placing them in Darfur as quickly as possible with a strong protection mandate, rather than a monitoring one ENDEND  In the mean time, it's going to take about year, at best, to get a UN peacekeeping force in place ENDEND  We're going to have to supply and rally, bridging money and forces for the AU throughout this year, because, since it's sort of in lameduck status, the Janjaweed recognize that AU forces are not particularly effective, they may become more and more of a target ENDEND  We're going to have to provide this successor UN force with our own lift and logistic assets ENDEND  We're going to have to provide our military hardware, like transport and attack helicopters, and so forth ENDEND  And, we're going to have to really force other countries like Canada, Australia, some of the European countries that are not engaged in peacekeeping in other places, or at least are not immediately involved in major activity in places like Iraq and Afghanistan, as we are, to deliver the troops that are needed ENDEND 
So, it is absolutely critical that we start focusing on this now ENDEND  The situation, as bad as it is, could deteriorate further ENDEND  This is something that is of interest, I think, to all of us, not just for humanitarian reasons, although when you read the accounts of women being raped when they are out collecting firewood, when you read just horrendous accounts of entire villages being decimated and children being murdered, that it just breaks your heart, and humanitarian concerns should be sufficient, but we also have a strong national security interest ENDEND  If you start seeing more and more failed states, more and more displaced persons, more and more refugees, all of that becomes a breeding ground for terrorist activity, it becomes a breeding ground for disease, and it creates refugees that put pressure on our own borders ENDEND  In an innerconnected world we can't insulate ourselves from these tragedies ENDEND  So, we're going to, over time, have to develop some strategy as the world's remaining superpower to address these issues, and Darfur is an important test case ENDEND  We've already failed one test in Rwanda, we shouldn't fail another ENDEND 
Anyway, if you are interested in the issues related to Darfur, you can always contact my office, or get on the website ENDEND  Your voice is obviously critical in this issue ENDEND  I appreciate you, as always listening in ENDEND  Thank you for downloading, and I will talk to you next week ENDEND  Bye bye ENDEND 

I want to start by thanking the Kaiser foundation for the work you've done not only on today's report, but on making these issues of media and family a part of the national conversation ENDEND 
This is a subject many of us come to not as politicians or policy makers, as but as parents most of all ENDEND 
Because it's one thing to discuss sex and violence on television within the larger context of the culture wars  as a values debate between First Amendment crusaders and those who believe government should decide what we can and cannot watch  but it's a another thing altogether to be faced with these issues while you're sitting in front of the TV with your child ENDEND 
I watch with my daughters, Sasha and Malia, and I can tell you that when we're in the middle of a family program and a commercial for Cialis comes on, it's more than troubling to find yourself wondering how you'll explain certain medical conditions that last longer than three hours to a fouryearold and a sevenyearold ENDEND 
From the time they're young, we try to instill in our children a sense of what's right and wrong; a sense of what's important, of what's worth striving for ENDEND  As best we can, we also try to shield them from the harsher elements of life, and introduce them to the realities of adulthood at the appropriate age ENDEND 
But the concern shared by so many parents today  a concern that frankly hasn't been taken seriously enough by some on the left  is that raising your children this way has become exceedingly difficult in a mass media culture that saturates our airwaves with a steady stream of sex, violence, and materialism ENDEND 
Revolutions in information and technology over the last few decades have caused this stream to grow exponentially, as we're bombarded at every turn with sounds and images from DVDs, iPods, video games, and websites that we can't always control ENDEND 
At the center of it all sits the television, which still consumes the vast majority of our media use  even more so for our children ENDEND  And as we're spending more free time immersed in this media culture, the amount of questionable content spilling across our screens is growing by the year ENDEND 
Still, it's important for us to realize that the real problem we're facing is not simply one of quantity, or even the existence of sex and violence in the media per se ENDEND 
After all, the adult content in Schindler's List is far different from the type on Desperate Housewives, and the violence in Saving Private Ryan is not the same as the kind our kids try to imitate in some of the most popular video games ENDEND 
Rather, as your study today demonstrates, the larger concern here is one of message; it's what the media is teaching our kids about what is ok and what is not; about how to treat others and how to treat themselves ENDEND 
It's a concern that mass media is contributing to an overall coarsening of our culture ENDEND 
That with all the time our children are spending in front of the television, with all the choices they have to see whatever they want whenever they want, the content of their viewing is not enriching their minds, but numbing them; not broadening intellectual curiosity or appreciation for the arts, but trivializing the important and desensitizing us to the tragic ENDEND 
It may seem to some that the effect on our children has been overstated ENDEND  But the studies coming in from the NIH and others show that the connection is real ENDEND  When children are exposed to sex without consequences, they're more likely to have it ENDEND 
When they are shown the risks and responsibilities that go along with sex, at least one major subgroup  AfricanAmerican youth  are more likely to abstain ENDEND  Mindless violence and macho aggression on television begets the same behavior in our kids ENDEND  And when eighty percent of AfricanAmerican teens in a city like Washington think that they'll be rich and over half think they'll be famous, it hurts to hear them say that the path to success lies with the hoop dreams and rap careers glorified on television ENDEND 
We don't teach our children that healthy relationships involve drunken, naked parties in a hot tub with strangers  but that's what they see when they turn on The Real World ENDEND  We don't teach them to express their anger by seeing how much blood they can draw with a round of ammo  but that's what they learn in the most popular video games ENDEND  And we don't teach our kids that the height of success is inheriting a family fortune to buy Gucci bags without ever working a serious day in your life  but that's how Paris Hilton gets by on The Simple Life ENDEND  You can say that kids know this isn't real, but when they're fed a steady diet of these depictions over and over again from the time they're very young, this behavior becomes acceptable  even normal ENDEND 
So what do we do about this? What do we do when bad television becomes the enemy of good parenting?
We start by turning off the TV altogether ENDEND  Our children now spend an average of three hours a day in front of the television  for AfricanAmerican children, it's four hours ENDEND  Two out of every three households have the TV on during meals ENDEND 
This is too much  period ENDEND  And so I think it would help if parents start setting down stricter rules on how much TV their kids watch and limit their hours ENDEND  I know this is difficult ENDEND  At the end of a long day, when Michelle and I are tired, it's easy to just sit the kids in front of the television and relax ENDEND 
But I think that as parents, we have an obligation to our children to turn off the TV, pick up a book, and read to them more often ENDEND 
Beyond that, when our kids do watch television, we should be watching it with them  this means finding programming that everyone can watch as a family and being there to answer any questions it may raise with our kids ENDEND 
Now, at a time when both parents are more likely to work longer hours outside the home, this is a lot easier said than done ENDEND  We try to compete with these media messages, but it's nearly impossible to be there every moment our kids are watching television ENDEND 
And so there's a broader responsibility here ENDEND 
We know that with the pervasiveness of mass media today  the existence of so many means of communication that are so easily accessible all over the world  it's very difficult to regulate our way out of this problem ENDEND  And for those of us who value our First Amendment freedoms  who value artistic expression  we wouldn't want to ENDEND 
But that doesn't mean we have to accept this coarsening of our culture ENDEND 
Decades ago, when television was still in its infancy, we provided broadcasters free use of the public airwaves, which they were to operate as trustees for the public ENDEND  And just last week, the Senate voted to set a final date for the transition to digital television ENDEND 
Today, we need to make it clear that the free use of the public airwaves continues to come with certain specific obligations ENDEND  But we also need to make it clear that for both broadcasters and their competitors there are larger civic obligations to the American public ENDEND  Obligations to reflect not the basest elements of American culture, but the profound and the proud ENDEND 
Obligations to seek not just the quick buck or the bottom line, but healthy discussion and debate in the public square of the information age ENDEND  Obligations to our children; to our families ENDEND 
Today, we have far more choice in what we watch than we could have ever imagined  more channels and more programming ENDEND  As we move further into the digital age, the transformation of entertainment will be even more dramatic than the one from stage to screen ENDEND 
And yet, with all these new choices for consumers, there has been remarkably little done to give parents the tools and the information necessary to make their own informed choices about what their children are watching ENDEND 
This is what the industry must do today ENDEND  As we move towards a digital environment, there is a golden opportunity for them to do it on their own  to use the latest in technology to give parents more information and more choice ENDEND 
For example, this technology could make it possible for parents to create their own family tier just by programming their television to block certain channels, block certain genres of programming like dramas, or block television at certain times of the day ENDEND  There's no reason the industry can't make it as easy to find familyfriendly television as it is to program TiVo ENDEND 
But if the industry fails to act  if it fails to give parents advanced controls and new choices  Congress will ENDEND 
I know that Senator Stevens and Senator Inouye are putting pressure on both broadcasters and cable companies to do a better job fighting indecency, and I'm fully behind their efforts to get the industry to change ENDEND  I also applaud their announcement that they will be convening a summit on these issues with the goal of achieving immediate, meaningful reforms ENDEND 
But I'd like to outline some additional reforms that I think can make a difference for parents today ENDEND 
First, parents should be able to get better information right away  by improving the voluntary rating system we currently have ENDEND  Right now, our television ratings involve nothing more than a tiny box containing some letters and numbers that flashes in the upper lefthand corner of the screen for a few seconds at the beginning of each program ENDEND  It's hard to understand and easy to miss ENDEND  Broadcasters must improve this system to include a fullscreen, detailed rating that gives parents a more precise understanding of exactly what content will be shown in the program ENDEND 
They must also ensure that promos for horror movies and ads for the show Las Vegas aren't being shown in the middle of a cartoon or a family sitcom with a more restrictive rating ENDEND 
Beyond simply blocking out negative messages, however, we also know from Kaiser's studies that television has the power to promote positive messages that can influence behavior and raise awareness ENDEND 
Public service announcements have actually led to reductions in teen pregnancy, and we should all be proud of the media initiative undertaken by the Kaiser Foundation with Viacom, BET, UPN and other networks to eradicate ignorance about HIV and AIDS ENDEND 
There has been a long debate about what obligations broadcasters will have to the public in this new digital age ENDEND  The FCC took a first step in defining these obligations by requiring that broadcasters air children's educational programming on all their digital streams ENDEND 
As they continue this process, the FCC must make sure they spell out these obligations before the transition to digital programming is complete ENDEND 
When they do this, they need to make sure that broadcasters have a concrete obligation to provide public service announcements at times when people can actually see them, as well as better coverage of elections ENDEND  They should donate the public service time to a thirdparty like the Ad Council that works with reputable nonprofits ENDEND  If they do not do this, Congress should ENDEND 
In addition, we should also fight to prevent any attempt to gut funding or support for the Public Broadcasting System  positive television with educational messages that generations of children have been raised on ENDEND 
Finally, there's current legislation out there that would promote further studies  like this one  which would study the effects of media on the health and development of our children ENDEND  This will provide parents with even more information, it's got bipartisan support in Congress, and I think it's a good idea to pursue ENDEND 
In Newton Minow's famous "Vast Wasteland" speech to the National Association of Television Broadcasters, he told them that,
"It is not enough to cater to the nation's whims  you must also serve the nation's needs ENDEND "
