Today, as so many generations have before, we gather on our National Mall to tell an essential part of our American story  one that has at times been overlooked  we come not just for today, but for all time ENDEND 
President and Mrs ENDEND  Bush; President Clinton; Vice President and Dr ENDEND  Biden; Chief Justice Roberts; Secretary Skorton; Reverend Butts; distinguished guests: Thank you ENDEND  Thank you for your leadership in making sure this tale is told ENDEND  We’re here in part because of you and because of all those Americans  the Civil War vets, the Civil Rights foot soldiers, the champions of this effort on Capitol Hill  who, for more than a century, kept the dream of this museum alive ENDEND 
That includes our leaders in Congress  Paul Ryan and Nancy Pelosi ENDEND  It includes one of my heroes, John Lewis, who, as he has so often, took the torch from those who came before him and brought us past the finish line ENDEND  It includes the philanthropists and benefactors and advisory members who have so generously given not only their money but their time ENDEND  It includes the Americans who offered up all the family keepsakes tucked away in Grandma’s attic ENDEND  And of course, it includes a man without whose vision and passion and persistence we would not be here today  Mr. Lonnie Bunch ENDEND 
What we can see of this building  the towering glass, the artistry of the metalwork  is surely a sight to behold ENDEND  But beyond the majesty of the building, what makes this occasion so special is the larger story it contains ENDEND  Below us, this building reaches down  feet, its roots spreading far wider and deeper than any tree on this Mall ENDEND  And on its lowest level, after you walk past remnants of a slave ship, after you reflect on the immortal declaration that “all men are created equal,” you can see a block of stone ENDEND  On top of this stone sits a historical marker, weathered by the ages ENDEND  That marker reads: “General Andrew Jackson and Henry Clay spoke from this slave block…during the year  ENDEND ”
I want you to think about this ENDEND  Consider what this artifact tells us about history, about how it’s told, and about what can be cast aside ENDEND  On a stone where day after day, for years, men and women were torn from their spouse or their child, shackled and bound, and bought and sold, and bid like cattle; on a stone worn down by the tragedy of over a thousand bare feet  for a long time, the only thing we considered important, the singular thing we once chose to commemorate as “history” with a plaque were the unmemorable speeches of two powerful men ENDEND 
And that block I think explains why this museum is so necessary ENDEND  Because that same object, reframed, put in context, tells us so much more ENDEND  As Americans, we rightfully passed on the tales of the giants who built this country; who led armies into battle and waged seminal debates in the halls of Congress and the corridors of power ENDEND  But too often, we ignored or forgot the stories of millions upon millions of others, who built this nation just as surely, whose humble eloquence, whose calloused hands, whose steady drive helped to create cities, erect industries, build the arsenals of democracy ENDEND 
And so this national museum helps to tell a richer and fuller story of who we are ENDEND  It helps us better understand the lives, yes, of the President, but also the slave; the industrialist, but also the porter; the keeper of the status quo, but also of the activist seeking to overthrow that status quo; the teacher or the cook, alongside the statesman ENDEND  And by knowing this other story, we better understand ourselves and each other ENDEND  It binds us together ENDEND  It reaffirms that all of us are America  that AfricanAmerican history is not somehow separate from our larger American story, it's not the underside of the American story, it is central to the American story ENDEND  That our glory derives not just from our most obvious triumphs, but how we’ve wrested triumph from tragedy, and how we've been able to remake ourselves, again and again and again, in accordance with our highest ideals ENDEND 
I, too, am America ENDEND 
The great historian John Hope Franklin, who helped to get this museum started, once said, “Good history is a good foundation for a better present and future ENDEND ” He understood the best history doesn’t just sit behind a glass case; it helps us to understand what’s outside the case ENDEND  The best history helps us recognize the mistakes that we’ve made and the dark corners of the human spirit that we need to guard against ENDEND  And, yes, a cleareyed view of history can make us uncomfortable, and shake us out of familiar narratives ENDEND  But it is precisely because of that discomfort that we learn and grow and harness our collective power to make this nation more perfect ENDEND 
That’s the American story that this museum tells  one of suffering and delight; one of fear but also of hope; of wandering in the wilderness and then seeing out on the horizon a glimmer of the Promised Land ENDEND 
It is in this embrace of truth, as best as we can know it, in the celebration of the entire American experience, where real patriotism lies ENDEND  As President Bush just said, a great nation doesn’t shy from the truth ENDEND  It strengthens us ENDEND  It emboldens us ENDEND  It should fortify us ENDEND  It is an act of patriotism to understand where we've been ENDEND  And this museum tells the story of so many patriots ENDEND 
Yes, African Americans have felt the cold weight of shackles and the stinging lash of the field whip ENDEND  But we’ve also dared to run north, and sing songs from Harriet Tubman’s hymnal ENDEND  We’ve buttoned up our Union Blues to join the fight for our freedom ENDEND  We’ve railed against injustice for decade upon decade  a lifetime of struggle, and progress, and enlightenment that we see etched in Frederick Douglass’s mighty, leonine gaze ENDEND 
Yes, this museum tells a story of people who felt the indignity, the small and large humiliations of a “whites only” sign, or wept at the side of Emmett Till’s coffin, or fell to their knees on shards of stained glass outside a church where four little girls died ENDEND  But it also tells the story of the black youth and white youth sitting alongside each other, straightbacked, so full of dignity on those lunch counter stools; the story of a sixyearold Ruby Bridges, pigtails, freshpressed dress, walking that gauntlet to get to school; Tuskegee airmen soaring the skies not just to beat a dictator, but to reaffirm the promise of our democracy  but remind us that all of us are created equal ENDEND 
This is the place to understand how protest and love of country don’t merely coexist but inform each other; how men can proudly win the gold for their country but still insist on raising a blackgloved fist; how we can wear “I Can’t Breathe” Tshirt and still grieve for fallen police officers ENDEND  Here’s the America where the razorsharp uniform of the Chairman of the Joint Chiefs of Staff belongs alongside the cape of the Godfather of Soul ENDEND  We have shown the world that we can float like butterflies and sting like bees; that we can rocket into space like Mae Jemison, steal home like Jackie, rock like Jimi, stir the pot like Richard Pryor; or we can be sick and tired of being sick and tired, like Fannie Lou Hamer, and still Rock Steady like Aretha Franklin ENDEND 
We are large, Walt Whitman told us, containing multitudes ENDEND  We are large, containing multitudes ENDEND  Full of contradictions ENDEND  That's America ENDEND  That's what makes us grow ENDEND  That's what makes us extraordinary ENDEND  And as is true for America, so is true for African American experience ENDEND  We're not a burden on America, or a stain on America, or an object of pity or charity for America ENDEND  We're America ENDEND 
And that's what this museum explains  the fact that our stories have shaped every corner of our culture ENDEND  The struggles for freedom that took place made our Constitution a real and living document, tested and shaped and deepened and made more profound its meaning for all people ENDEND  The story told here doesn’t just belong to black Americans; it belongs to all Americans  for the AfricanAmerican experience has been shaped just as much by Europeans and Asians and Native Americans and Latinos ENDEND  We have informed each other ENDEND  We are polyglot, a stew ENDEND 
Scripture promised that if we lift up the oppressed, then our light will rise in the darkness, and our night will become like the noonday ENDEND  And the story contained in this museum makes those words prophecy ENDEND  And that’s what this day is about ENDEND  That’s what this museum is about ENDEND  I, too, am America ENDEND  It is a glorious story, the one that's told here ENDEND  It is complicated and it is messy and it is full of contradictions, as all great stories are, as Shakespeare is, as Scripture is ENDEND  And it’s a story that perhaps needs to be told now more than ever ENDEND 
A museum alone will not alleviate poverty in every inner city or every rural hamlet ENDEND  It won't eliminate gun violence from all our neighborhoods, or immediately ensure that justice is always colorblind ENDEND  It won't wipe away every instance of discrimination in a job interview or a sentencing hearing or folks trying to rent an apartment ENDEND  Those things are up to us, the decisions and choices we make ENDEND  It requires speaking out, and organizing, and voting, until our values are fully reflected in our laws and our policies and our communities ENDEND 
But what this museum does show us is that in even the face of oppression, even in the face of unimaginable difficulty, America has moved forward ENDEND  And so this museum provides context for the debates of our times ENDEND  It illuminates them and gives us some sense of how they evolved, and perhaps keeps them in proportion ENDEND  Perhaps it can help a white visitor understand the pain and anger of demonstrators in places like Tulsa and Charlotte ENDEND  But it can also help black visitors appreciate the fact that not only is this younger generation carrying on traditions of the past but, within the white communities across this nation we see the sincerity of law enforcement officers and officials who, in fits and starts, are struggling to understand, and are trying to do the right thing ENDEND 
It reminds us that routine discrimination and Jim Crow aren't ancient history, it's just a blink in the eye of history ENDEND  It was just yesterday ENDEND  And so we should not be surprised that not all the healing is done ENDEND  We shouldn’t despair that it’s not all solved ENDEND  And knowing the larger story should instead remind us of just how remarkable the changes that have taken place truly are  just in my lifetime  and thereby inspire us to further progress ENDEND 
And so hopefully this museum can help us talk to each other ENDEND  And more importantly, listen to each other ENDEND  And most importantly, see each other ENDEND  Black and white and Latino and Native American and Asian American  see how our stories are bound together ENDEND  And bound together with women in America, and workers in America, and entrepreneurs in America, and LGBT Americans ENDEND  And for young people who didn’t live through the struggles represented here, I hope you draw strength from the changes that have taken place ENDEND  Come here and see the power of your own agency ENDEND  See how young John Lewis was ENDEND  These were children who transformed a nation in a blink of an eye ENDEND  Young people, come here and see your ability to make your mark ENDEND 
The very fact of this day does not prove that America is perfect, but it does validate the ideas of our founding, that this country born of change, this country born of revolution, this country of we, the people, this country can get better ENDEND 
And that’s why we celebrate, mindful that our work is not yet done; mindful that we are but on a waystation on this common journey towards freedom ENDEND  And how glorious it is that we enshrine it here, on some of our nation’s most hallowed ground  the same place where lives were once traded but also where hundreds of thousands of Americans, of all colors and creeds, once marched ENDEND  How joyful it is that this story take its rightful place  alongside Jefferson who declared our independence, and Washington who made it real, and alongside Lincoln who saved our union, and the GIs who defended it; alongside a new monument to a King, gazing outward, summoning us toward that mountaintop ENDEND  How righteous it is that with tell this story here ENDEND 
For almost eight years, I have been blessed with the extraordinary honor of serving you in this office ENDEND  Time and again, I’ve flown low over this mall on Marine One, often with Michelle and our daughters ENDEND  And President Clinton, President Bush, they’ll tell you it is incredible sight ENDEND  We pass right across the Washington Monument  it feels like you can reach out and touch it ENDEND  And at night, if you turn the other way, you don't just see the Lincoln Memorial, Old Abe is lit up and you can see him, his spirit glowing from that building ENDEND  And we don’t have many trips left ENDEND  But over the years, I’ve always been comforted as I’ve watched this museum rise from this earth into this remarkable tribute ENDEND  Because I know that years from now, like all of you, Michelle and I will be able to come here to this museum, and not just bring our kids but hopefully our grandkids ENDEND  I imagine holding a little hand of somebody and tell them the stories that are enshrined here ENDEND 
And in the years that follow, they’ll be able to do the same ENDEND  And then we’ll go to the Lincoln Memorial and we'll take in the view atop the Washington Monument ENDEND  And together, we’ll learn about ourselves, as Americans  our sufferings, our delights, and our triumphs ENDEND  And we’ll walk away better for it, better because the better grasp of history ENDEND  We'll walk away that much more in love with this country, the only place on Earth where this story could have unfolded ENDEND 
It is a monument, no less than the others on this Mall, to the deep and abiding love for this country, and the ideals upon which it is founded ENDEND  For we, too, are America ENDEND 
So enough talk ENDEND  President Bush is timing me ENDEND  He had the overunder at  ENDEND  Let us now open this museum to the world ENDEND  Today, we have with us a family that reflects the arc of our progress: the Bonner family  four generations in all, starting with gorgeous sevenyearold Christine and going up to gorgeous yearold Ruth ENDEND 
Now, Ruth’s father, Elijah Odom, was born into servitude in Mississippi ENDEND  He was born a slave ENDEND  As a young boy, he ran, though, to his freedom ENDEND  He lived through Reconstruction and he lived through Jim Crow ENDEND  But he went on to farm, and graduate from medical school, and gave life to the beautiful family that we see today  with a spirit reflected in beautiful Christine, free and equal in the laws of her country and in the eyes of God ENDEND 
So in a brief moment, their family will join us in ringing a bell from the First Baptist Church in Virginia  one of the oldest black churches in America, founded under a grove of trees in  ENDEND  And the sound of this bell will be echoed by others in houses of worship and town squares all across this country  an echo of the ringing bells that signaled Emancipation more than a century and a half ago; the sound, and the anthem, of American freedom ENDEND 
God bless you all ENDEND  God bless the United States of America ENDEND 


From the depths of the greatest financial crisis of our time, we coordinated our response to avoid further catastrophe and return the global economy to growth ENDEND  We’ve taken away terrorist safe havens, strengthened the nonproliferation regime, resolved the Iranian nuclear issue through diplomacy ENDEND  We opened relations with Cuba, helped Colombia end Latin America’s longest warm, and we welcome a democratically elected leader of Myanmar to this Assembly ENDEND  Our assistance is helping people feed themselves, care for the sick, power communities across Africa, and promote models of development rather than dependence ENDEND  And we have made international institutions like the World Bank and the International Monetary Fund more representative, while establishing a framework to protect our planet from the ravages of climate change ENDEND 
This is important work ENDEND  It has made a real difference in the lives of our people ENDEND  And it could not have happened had we not worked together ENDEND  And yet, around the globe we are seeing the same forces of global integration that have made us interdependent also expose deep fault lines in the existing international order ENDEND 
We see it in the headlines every day ENDEND  Around the world, refugees flow across borders in flight from brutal conflict ENDEND  Financial disruptions continue to weigh upon our workers and entire communities ENDEND  Across vast swaths of the Middle East, basic security, basic order has broken down ENDEND  We see too many governments muzzling journalists, and quashing dissent, and censoring the flow of information ENDEND  Terrorist networks use social media to prey upon the minds of our youth, endangering open societies and spurring anger against innocent immigrants and Muslims ENDEND  Powerful nations contest the constraints placed on them by international law ENDEND 
This is the paradox that defines our world today ENDEND  A quarter century after the end of the Cold War, the world is by many measures less violent and more prosperous than ever before, and yet our societies are filled with uncertainty, and unease, and strife ENDEND  Despite enormous progress, as people lose trust in institutions, governing becomes more difficult and tensions between nations become more quick to surface ENDEND 
And so I believe that at this moment we all face a choice ENDEND  We can choose to press forward with a better model of cooperation and integration ENDEND  Or we can retreat into a world sharply divided, and ultimately in conflict, along ageold lines of nation and tribe and race and religion ENDEND 
I want to suggest to you today that we must go forward, and not backward ENDEND  I believe that as imperfect as they are, the principles of open markets and accountable governance, of democracy and human rights and international law that we have forged remain the firmest foundation for human progress in this century ENDEND  I make this argument not based on theory or ideology, but on facts  facts that all too often, we forget in the immediacy of current events ENDEND 
Here’s the most important fact: The integration of our global economy has made life better for billions of men, women and children ENDEND  Over the last  years, the number of people living in extreme poverty has been cut from nearly  percent of humanity to under  percent ENDEND  That's unprecedented ENDEND  And it's not an abstraction ENDEND  It means children have enough to eat; mothers don’t die in childbirth ENDEND 
Meanwhile, cracking the genetic code promises to cure diseases that have plagued us for centuries ENDEND  The Internet can deliver the entirety of human knowledge to a young girl in a remote village on a single handheld device ENDEND  In medicine and in manufacturing, in education and communications, we’re experiencing a transformation of how human beings live on a scale that recalls the revolutions in agriculture and industry ENDEND  And as a result, a person born today is more likely to be healthy, to live longer, and to have access to opportunity than at any time in human history ENDEND 
Moreover, the collapse of colonialism and communism has allowed more people than ever before to live with the freedom to choose their leaders ENDEND  Despite the real and troubling areas where freedom appears in retreat, the fact remains that the number of democracies around the world has nearly doubled in the last  years ENDEND 
In remote corners of the world, citizens are demanding respect for the dignity of all people no matter their gender, or race, or religion, or disability, or sexual orientation, and those who deny others dignity are subject to public reproach ENDEND  An explosion of social media has given ordinary people more ways to express themselves, and has raised people’s expectations for those of us in power ENDEND  Indeed, our international order has been so successful that we take it as a given that great powers no longer fight world wars; that the end of the Cold War lifted the shadow of nuclear Armageddon; that the battlefields of Europe have been replaced by peaceful union; that China and India remain on a path of remarkable growth ENDEND 
I say all this not to whitewash the challenges we face, or to suggest complacency ENDEND  Rather, I believe that we need to acknowledge these achievements in order to summon the confidence to carry this progress forward and to make sure that we do not abandon those very things that have delivered this progress ENDEND 
In order to move forward, though, we do have to acknowledge that the existing path to global integration requires a course correction ENDEND  As too often, those trumpeting the benefits of globalization have ignored inequality within and among nations; have ignored the enduring appeal of ethnic and sectarian identities; have left international institutions illequipped, underfunded, underresourced, in order to handle transnational challenges ENDEND 
And as these real problems have been neglected, alternative visions of the world have pressed forward both in the wealthiest countries and in the poorest: religious fundamentalism; the politics of ethnicity, or tribe, or sect; aggressive nationalism; a crude populism  sometimes from the far left, but more often from the far right  which seeks to restore what they believe was a better, simpler age free of outside contamination ENDEND 
We cannot dismiss these visions ENDEND  They are powerful ENDEND  They reflect dissatisfaction among too many of our citizens ENDEND  I do not believe those visions can deliver security or prosperity over the long term, but I do believe that these visions fail to recognize, at a very basic level, our common humanity ENDEND  Moreover, I believe that the acceleration of travel and technology and telecommunications  together with a global economy that depends on a global supply chain  makes it selfdefeating ultimately for those who seek to reverse this progress ENDEND  Today, a nation ringed by walls would only imprison itself ENDEND 
So the answer cannot be a simple rejection of global integration ENDEND  Instead, we must work together to make sure the benefits of such integration are broadly shared, and that the disruptions  economic, political, and cultural  that are caused by integration are squarely addressed ENDEND  This is not the place for a detailed policy blueprint, but let me offer in broad strokes those areas where I believe we must do better together ENDEND 
It starts with making the global economy work better for all people and not just for those at the top ENDEND  While open markets, capitalism have raised standards of living around the globe, globalization combined with rapid progress and technology has also weakened the position of workers and their ability to secure a decent wage ENDEND  In advanced economies like my own, unions have been undermined, and many manufacturing jobs have disappeared ENDEND  Often, those who benefit most from globalization have used their political power to further undermine the position of workers ENDEND 
In developing countries, labor organizations have often been suppressed, and the growth of the middle class has been held back by corruption and underinvestment ENDEND  Mercantilist policies pursued by governments with exportdriven models threaten to undermine the consensus that underpins global trade ENDEND  And meanwhile, global capital is too often unaccountable  nearly  trillion dollars stashed away in tax havens, a shadow banking system that grows beyond the reach of effective oversight ENDEND 
A world in which one percent of humanity controls as much wealth as the other  percent will never be stable ENDEND  I understand that the gaps between rich and poor are not new, but just as the child in a slum today can see the skyscraper nearby, technology now allows any person with a smartphone to see how the most privileged among us live and the contrast between their own lives and others ENDEND  Expectations rise, then, faster than governments can deliver, and a pervasive sense of injustice undermine people’s faith in the system ENDEND 
So how do we fix this imbalance? We cannot unwind integration any more than we can stuff technology back into a box ENDEND  Nor can we look to failed models of the past ENDEND  If we start resorting to trade wars, market distorting subsidies, beggar thy neighbor policies, an overreliance on natural resources instead of innovation  these approaches will make us poorer, collectively, and they are more like to lead to conflict ENDEND  And the stark contrast between, say, the success of the Republic of Korea and the wasteland of North Korea shows that central, planned control of the economy is a dead end ENDEND 
But I do believe there’s another path  one that fuels growth and innovation, and offers the clearest route to individual opportunity and national success ENDEND  It does not require succumbing to a soulless capitalism that benefits only the few, but rather recognizes that economies are more successful when we close the gap between rich and poor, and growth is broadly based ENDEND  And that means respecting the rights of workers so they can organize into independent unions and earn a living wage ENDEND  It means investing in our people  their skills, their education, their capacity to take an idea and turn it into a business ENDEND  It means strengthening the safety net that protects our people from hardship and allows them to take more risks  to look for a new job, or start a new venture ENDEND 
These are the policies that I’ve pursued here in the United States, and with clear results ENDEND  American businesses have created now  million new jobs ENDEND  After the recession, the top one percent of Americans were capturing more than  percent of income growth ENDEND  But today, that's down to about half ENDEND  Last year, poverty in this country fell at the fastest rate in nearly  years ENDEND  And with further investment in infrastructure and early childhood education and basic research, I’m confident that such progress will continue ENDEND 
So just as I’ve pursued these measures here at home, so has the United States worked with many nations to curb the excesses of capitalism  not to punish wealth, but to prevent repeated crises that can destroy it ENDEND  That’s why we’ve worked with other nations to create higher and clearer standards for banking and taxation  because a society that asks less of oligarchs than ordinary citizens will rot from within ENDEND  That’s why we’ve pushed for transparency and cooperation in rooting out corruption, and tracking illicit dollars, because markets create more jobs when they're fueled by hard work, and not the capacity to extort a bribe ENDEND  That’s why we’ve worked to reach trade agreements that raise labor standards and raise environmental standards, as we've done with the TransPacific Partnership, so that the benefits are more broadly shared ENDEND 
And just as we benefit by combating inequality within our countries, I believe advanced economies still need to do more to close the gap between rich and poor nations around the globe ENDEND  This is difficult politically ENDEND  It's difficult to spend on foreign assistance ENDEND  But I do not believe this is charity ENDEND  For the small fraction of what we spent at war in Iraq we could support institutions so that fragile states don’t collapse in the first place, and invest in emerging economies that become markets for our goods ENDEND  It's not just the right thing to do, it's the smart thing to do ENDEND 
And that’s why we need to follow through on our efforts to combat climate change ENDEND  If we don't act boldly, the bill that could come due will be mass migrations, and cities submerged and nations displaced, and food supplies decimated, and conflicts born of despair ENDEND  The Paris Agreement gives us a framework to act, but only if we scale up our ambition ENDEND  And there must be a sense of urgency about bringing the agreement into force, and helping poorer countries leapfrog destructive forms of energy ENDEND 
So, for the wealthiest countries, a Green Climate Fund should only be the beginning ENDEND  We need to invest in research and provide market incentives to develop new technologies, and then make these technologies accessible and affordable for poorer countries ENDEND  And only then can we continue lifting all people up from poverty without condemning our children to a planet beyond their capacity to repair ENDEND 
So we need new models for the global marketplace, models that are inclusive and sustainable ENDEND  And in the same way, we need models of governance that are inclusive and accountable to ordinary people ENDEND 
I recognize not every country in this hall is going to follow the same model of governance ENDEND  I do not think that America can  or should  impose our system of government on other countries ENDEND  But there appears to be growing contest between authoritarianism and liberalism right now ENDEND  And I want everybody to understand, I am not neutral in that contest ENDEND  I believe in a liberal political order  an order built not just through elections and representative government, but also through respect for human rights and civil society, and independent judiciaries and the rule of law ENDEND 
I know that some countries, which now recognize the power of free markets, still reject the model of free societies ENDEND  And perhaps those of us who have been promoting democracy feel somewhat discouraged since the end of the Cold War, because we've learned that liberal democracy will not just wash across the globe in a single wave ENDEND  It turns out building accountable institutions is hard work  the work of generations ENDEND  The gains are often fragile ENDEND  Sometimes we take one step forward and then two steps back ENDEND  In countries held together by borders drawn by colonial powers, with ethnic enclaves and tribal divisions, politics and elections can sometimes appear to be a zerosum game ENDEND  And so, given the difficulty in forging true democracy in the face of these pressures, it’s no surprise that some argue the future favors the strongman, a topdown model, rather than strong, democratic institutions ENDEND 
But I believe this thinking is wrong ENDEND  I believe the road of true democracy remains the better path ENDEND  I believe that in the st century, economies can only grow to a certain point until they need to open up  because entrepreneurs need to access information in order to invent; young people need a global education in order to thrive; independent media needs to check the abuses of power ENDEND  Without this evolution, ultimately expectations of people will not be met; suppression and stagnation will set in ENDEND  And history shows that strongmen are then left with two paths  permanent crackdown, which sparks strife at home, or scapegoating enemies abroad, which can lead to war ENDEND 
Now, I will admit, my belief that governments serve the individual, and not the other way around, is shaped by America’s story ENDEND  Our nation began with a promise of freedom that applied only to the few ENDEND  But because of our democratic Constitution, because of our Bill of Rights, because of our ideals, ordinary people were able to organize, and march, and protest, and ultimately, those ideals won out  opened doors for women and minorities and workers in ways that made our economy more productive and turned our diversity into a strength; that gave innovators the chance to transform every area of human endeavor; that made it possible for someone like me to be elected President of the United States ENDEND 
So, yes, my views are shaped by the specific experiences of America, but I do not think this story is unique to America ENDEND  Look at the transformation that's taken place in countries as different as Japan and Chile, Indonesia, Botswana ENDEND  The countries that have succeeded are ones in which people feel they have a stake ENDEND 
In Europe, the progress of those countries in the former Soviet bloc that embraced democracy stand in clear contrast to those that did not ENDEND  After all, the people of Ukraine did not take to the streets because of some plot imposed from abroad ENDEND  They took to the streets because their leadership was for sale and they had no recourse ENDEND  They demanded change because they saw life get better for people in the Baltics and in Poland, societies that were more liberal, and democratic, and open than their own ENDEND 
So those of us who believe in democracy, we need to speak out forcefully, because both the facts and history, I believe, are on our side ENDEND  That doesn’t mean democracies are without flaws ENDEND  It does mean that the cure for what ails our democracies is greater engagement by our citizens  not less ENDEND 
Yes, in America, there is too much money in politics; too much entrenched partisanship; too little participation by citizens, in part because of a patchwork of laws that makes it harder to vote ENDEND  In Europe, a wellintentioned Brussels often became too isolated from the normal push and pull of national politics ENDEND  Too often, in capitals, decisionmakers have forgotten that democracy needs to be driven by civic engagement from the bottom up, not governance by experts from the top down ENDEND  And so these are real problems, and as leaders of democratic governments make the case for democracy abroad, we better strive harder to set a better example at home ENDEND 
Moreover, every country will organize its government informed by centuries of history, and the circumstances of geography, and the deeply held beliefs of its people ENDEND  So I recognize a traditional society may value unity and cohesion more than a diverse country like my own, which was founded upon what, at the time, was a radical idea  the idea of the liberty of individual human beings endowed with certain Godgiven rights ENDEND  But that does not mean that ordinary people in Asia, or Africa, or the Middle East somehow prefer arbitrary rule that denies them a voice in the decisions that can shape their lives ENDEND  I believe that spirit is universal ENDEND  And if any of you doubt the universality of that desire, listen to the voices of young people everywhere who call out for freedom, and dignity, and the opportunity to control their own lives ENDEND 
This leads me to the third thing we need to do: We must reject any forms of fundamentalism, or racism, or a belief in ethnic superiority that makes our traditional identities irreconcilable with modernity ENDEND  Instead we need to embrace the tolerance that results from respect of all human beings ENDEND 
It’s a truism that global integration has led to a collision of cultures; trade, migration, the Internet, all these things can challenge and unsettle our most cherished identities ENDEND  We see liberal societies express opposition when women choose to cover themselves ENDEND  We see protests responding to Western newspaper cartoons that caricature the Prophet Muhammad ENDEND  In a world that left the age of empire behind, we see Russia attempting to recover lost glory through force ENDEND  Asian powers debate competing claims of history ENDEND  And in Europe and the United States, you see people wrestle with concerns about immigration and changing demographics, and suggesting that somehow people who look different are corrupting the character of our countries ENDEND 
Now, there’s no easy answer for resolving all these social forces, and we must respect the meaning that people draw from their own traditions  from their religion, from their ethnicity, from their sense of nationhood ENDEND  But I do not believe progress is possible if our desire to preserve our identities gives way to an impulse to dehumanize or dominate another group ENDEND  If our religion leads us to persecute those of another faith, if we jail or beat people who are gay, if our traditions lead us to prevent girls from going to school, if we discriminate on the basis of race or tribe or ethnicity, then the fragile bonds of civilization will fray ENDEND  The world is too small, we are too packed together, for us to be able to resort to those old ways of thinking ENDEND 
We see this mindset in too many parts of the Middle East ENDEND  There, so much of the collapse in order has been fueled because leaders sought legitimacy not because of policies or programs but by resorting to persecuting political opposition, or demonizing other religious sects, by narrowing the public space to the mosque, where in too many places perversions of a great faith were tolerated ENDEND  These forces built up for years, and are now at work helping to fuel both Syria’s tragic civil war and the mindless, medieval menace of ISIL ENDEND 
The mindset of sectarianism, and extremism, and bloodletting, and retribution that has been taking place will not be quickly reversed ENDEND  And if we are honest, we understand that no external power is going to be able to force different religious communities or ethnic communities to coexist for long ENDEND  But I do believe we have to be honest about the nature of these conflicts, and our international community must continue to work with those who seek to build rather than to destroy ENDEND 
And there is a military component to that ENDEND  It means being united and relentless in destroying networks like ISIL, which show no respect for human life ENDEND  But it also means that in a place like Syria, where there’s no ultimate military victory to be won, we’re going to have to pursue the hard work of diplomacy that aims to stop the violence, and deliver aid to those in need, and support those who pursue a political settlement and can see those who are not like themselves as worthy of dignity and respect ENDEND 
Across the region’s conflicts, we have to insist that all parties recognize a common humanity and that nations end proxy wars that fuel disorder ENDEND  Because until basic questions are answered about how communities coexist, the embers of extremism will continue to burn, countless human beings will suffer  most of all in that region  but extremism will continue to be exported overseas ENDEND  And the world is too small for us to simply be able to build a wall and prevent it from affecting our own societies ENDEND 
And what is true in the Middle East is true for all of us ENDEND  Surely, religious traditions can be honored and upheld while teaching young people science and math, rather than intolerance ENDEND  Surely, we can sustain our unique traditions while giving women their full and rightful role in the politics and economics of a nation ENDEND  Surely, we can rally our nations to solidarity while recognizing equal treatment for all communities  whether it’s a religious minority in Myanmar, or an ethnic minority in Burundi, or a racial minority right here in the United States ENDEND  And surely, Israelis and Palestinians will be better off if Palestinians reject incitement and recognize the legitimacy of Israel, but Israel recognizes that it cannot permanently occupy and settle Palestinian land ENDEND  We all have to do better as leaders in tamping down, rather than encouraging, a notion of identity that leads us to diminish others ENDEND 
And this leads me to the fourth and final thing we need to do, and that is sustain our commitment to international cooperation rooted in the rights and responsibilities of nations ENDEND 
As President of the United States, I know that for most of human history, power has not been unipolar ENDEND  The end of the Cold War may have led too many to forget this truth ENDEND  I’ve noticed as President that at times, both America’s adversaries and some of our allies believe that all problems were either caused by Washington or could be solved by Washington  and perhaps too many in Washington believed that as well ENDEND  But I believe America has been a rare superpower in human history insofar as it has been willing to think beyond narrow selfinterest; that while we’ve made our share of mistakes over these last  years  and I’ve acknowledged some  we have strived, sometimes at great sacrifice, to align better our actions with our ideals ENDEND  And as a consequence, I believe we have been a force for good ENDEND 
We have secured allies ENDEND  We’ve acted to protect the vulnerable ENDEND  We supported human rights and welcomed scrutiny of our own actions ENDEND  We’ve bound our power to international laws and institutions ENDEND  When we've made mistakes, we've tried to acknowledge them ENDEND  We have worked to roll back poverty and hunger and disease beyond our borders, not just within our borders ENDEND 
I'm proud of that ENDEND  But I also know that we can't do this alone ENDEND  And I believe that if we're to meet the challenges of this century, we are all going to have to do more to build up international capacity ENDEND  We cannot escape the prospect of nuclear war unless we all commit to stopping the spread of nuclear weapons and pursuing a world without them ENDEND 
When Iran agrees to accept constraints on its nuclear program that enhances global security and enhances Iran's ability to work with other nations ENDEND  On the other hand, when North Korea tests a bomb that endangers all of us ENDEND  And any country that breaks this basic bargain must face consequences ENDEND  And those nations with these weapons, like the United States, have a unique responsibility to pursue the path of reducing our stockpiles, and reaffirming basic norms like the commitment to never test them again ENDEND 
We can't combat a disease like Zika that recognizes no borders  mosquitoes don't respect walls  unless we make permanent the same urgency that we brought to bear against Ebola  by strengthening our own systems of public health, by investing in cures and rolling back the root causes of disease, and helping poorer countries develop a public health infrastructure ENDEND 
We can only eliminate extreme poverty if the sustainable development goals that we have set are more than words on paper ENDEND  Human ingenuity now gives us the capacity to feed the hungry and give all of our children  including our girls  the education that is the foundation for opportunity in our world ENDEND  But we have to put our money where our mouths are ENDEND 
And we can only realize the promise of this institution’s founding  to replace the ravages of war with cooperation  if powerful nations like my own accept constraints ENDEND  Sometimes I'm criticized in my own country for professing a belief in international norms and multilateral institutions ENDEND  But I am convinced that in the long run, giving up some freedom of action  not giving up our ability to protect ourselves or pursue our core interests, but binding ourselves to international rules over the long term  enhances our security ENDEND  And I think that's not just true for us ENDEND 
If Russia continues to interfere in the affairs of its neighbors, it may be popular at home, it may fuel nationalist fervor for a time, but over time it is also going to diminish its stature and make its borders less secure ENDEND  In the South China Sea, a peaceful resolution of disputes offered by law will mean far greater stability than the militarization of a few rocks and reefs ENDEND 
We are all stakeholders in this international system, and it calls upon all of us to invest in the success of institutions to which we belong ENDEND  And the good news is, is that many nations have shown what kind of progress is possible when we make those commitments ENDEND  Consider what we’ve accomplished here over the past few years ENDEND 
Together, we mobilized some , additional troops for United Nations  peacekeeping, making them nimble, better equipped, better prepared to deal with emergencies ENDEND  Together, we established an Open Government Partnership so that, increasingly, transparency empowers more and more people around the globe ENDEND  And together, now, we have to open our hearts and do more to help refugees who are desperate for a home ENDEND 
We should all welcome the pledges of increased assistance that have been made at this General Assembly gathering ENDEND  I'll be discussing that more this afternoon ENDEND  But we have to follow through, even when the politics are hard ENDEND  Because in the eyes of innocent men and women and children who, through no fault of their own, have had to flee everything that they know, everything that they love, we have to have the empathy to see ourselves ENDEND  We have to imagine what it would be like for our family, for our children, if the unspeakable happened to us ENDEND  And we should all understand that, ultimately, our world will be more secure if we are prepared to help those in need and the nations who are carrying the largest burden with respect to accommodating these refugees ENDEND 
There are a lot of nations right now that are doing the right thing ENDEND  But many nations  particularly those blessed with wealth and the benefits of geography  that can do more to offer a hand, even if they also insist that refugees who come to our countries have to do more to adapt to the customs and conventions of the communities that are now providing them a home ENDEND 
Let me conclude by saying that I recognize history tells a different story than the one that I've talked about here today ENDEND  There's a much darker and more cynical view of history that we can adopt ENDEND  Human beings are too often motivated by greed and by power ENDEND  Big countries for most of history have pushed smaller ones around ENDEND  Tribes and ethnic groups and nation states have very often found it most convenient to define themselves by what they hate and not just those ideas that bind them together ENDEND 
Time and again, human beings have believed that they finally arrived at a period of enlightenment only to repeat, then, cycles of conflict and suffering ENDEND  Perhaps that's our fate ENDEND  We have to remember that the choices of individual human beings led to repeated world war ENDEND  But we also have to remember that the choices of individual human beings created a United Nations, so that a war like that would never happen again ENDEND  Each of us as leaders, each nation can choose to reject those who appeal to our worst impulses and embrace those who appeal to our best ENDEND  For we have shown that we can choose a better history ENDEND 
Sitting in a prison cell, a young Martin Luther King, Jr ENDEND  wrote that, Human progress never rolls  on the wheels of inevitability; it comes through the tireless efforts of men willing to be coworkers with God ENDEND ” And during the course of these eight years, as I've traveled to many of your nations, I have seen that spirit in our young people, who are more educated and more tolerant, and more inclusive and more diverse, and more creative than our generation; who are more empathetic and compassionate towards their fellow human beings than previous generations ENDEND  And, yes, some of that comes with the idealism of youth ENDEND  But it also comes with young people’s access to information about other peoples and places  an understanding unique in human history that their future is bound with the fates of other human beings on the other side of the world ENDEND 
I think of the thousands of health care workers from around the world who volunteered to fight Ebola ENDEND  I remember the young entrepreneurs I met who are now starting new businesses in Cuba, the parliamentarians who used to be just a few years ago political prisoners in Myanmar ENDEND  I think of the girls who have braved taunts or violence just to go to school in Afghanistan, and the university students who started programs online to reject the extremism of organizations like ISIL ENDEND  I draw strength from the young Americans  entrepreneurs, activists, soldiers, new citizens  who are remaking our nation once again, who are unconstrained by old habits and old conventions, and unencumbered by what is, but are instead ready to seize what ought to be ENDEND 
My own family is a made up of the flesh and blood and traditions and cultures and faiths from a lot of different parts of the world  just as America has been built by immigrants from every shore ENDEND  And in my own life, in this country, and as President, I have learned that our identities do not have to be defined by putting someone else down, but can be enhanced by lifting somebody else up ENDEND  They don’t have to be defined in opposition to others, but rather by a belief in liberty and equality and justice and fairness ENDEND 
And the embrace of these principles as universal doesn't weaken my particular pride, my particular love for America  it strengthens it ENDEND  My belief that these ideals apply everywhere doesn’t lessen my commitment to help those who look like me, or pray as I do, or pledge allegiance to my flag ENDEND  But my faith in those principles does force me to expand my moral imagination and to recognize that I can best serve my own people, I can best look after my own daughters, by making sure that my actions seek what is right for all people and all children, and your daughters and your sons ENDEND 
This is what I believe: that all of us can be coworkers with God ENDEND  And our leadership, and our governments, and this United Nations should reflect this irreducible truth ENDEND 
Thank you very much ENDEND 

Good morning, everybody ENDEND  I want to say a few words about the explosions that occurred here in New York City and New Jersey and the other devices that have been found in New Jersey ENDEND  I’ve been monitoring the situation closely and receiving frequent updates from my team ENDEND  And I’ve just been briefed again by FBI Director Comey ENDEND  In addition, I've had a chance to speak with Governors Cuomo and Christie, as well as Mayor de Blasio ENDEND 
We’ve seen what was apparently a pipe bomb go off in New Jersey, in Seaside Park, where it could have seriously injured our United States   Marines and spectators who were there for a race ENDEND  The bombing in the Chelsea neighborhood, here in New York, injured more than two dozen people ENDEND  We are extremely fortunate and grateful that nobody was killed ENDEND  And our prayers go out to all those who have been injured ENDEND  We want to wish them a speedy recovery ENDEND 
I especially want to commend all the outstanding police and first responders in both New York City and New Jersey for their extraordinary professionalism and their quick response, which surely prevented even more people from being hurt, and ensured that people got assistance quickly ENDEND 
The investigation is moving rapidly, and as is my practice, I’m going to leave it to the FBI and law enforcement to provide details ENDEND  I think everybody is aware at this point that there is a person of interest who is the focus of the investigation ENDEND  And the FBI can give you further details in terms of how that is proceeding ENDEND 
I told Governors Cuomo and Christie and Mayor de Blasio that they and their teams will continue to have all federal support as they move ahead with their investigations, and tracking down every lead, and working to keep the people of this city and of this region safe ENDEND  Law enforcement is asking for the help of the community ENDEND  And so to everybody in this region, I want to repeat what we've said before: If you see something suspicious, then you need to say something  contact local law enforcement ENDEND 
In the meantime, I would ask that the press try to refrain from getting out ahead of the investigation ENDEND  I am extraordinarily happy with the cooperation that's been taking place between the FBI and state and local law enforcement officials ENDEND  They are moving smartly on this investigation ENDEND  It does not help if false reports or incomplete information is out there ENDEND  So try to, as much as possible, stick to what our investigators say, because they actually know what they're talking about ENDEND 
Meanwhile, I know that the United Nations meetings here every year already create an additional workload for New York ENDEND  But given the United Nations  meetings, we also have a particularly high level of federal resources here to help as needed ENDEND  We’re going to make sure that everybody is working together seamlessly, as one team, to get to the bottom of what happened, to find those responsible, and to make sure that justice is done ENDEND 
Meanwhile, while all this is going on in New York and New Jersey, we’re also focused on the stabbing attack at the shopping mall in Minnesota ENDEND  At this point, we see no connection between that incident and what happened here in New York and New Jersey ENDEND  Our attention there is on the people who were injured ENDEND  And again, we are very grateful that no one lost their life ENDEND  Thanks to the quick action of a brave offduty police officer, the suspect was killed and we avoided more people being hurt ENDEND 
I had a chance also to speak with Governor Dayton this morning ENDEND  I assured him that we will provide all the assistance that he needs in the investigation ENDEND  The FBI is investigating the Minnesota incident as a potential act of terrorism ENDEND  We will direct the full resources of the federal government to make sure that the investigation goes forward aggressively ENDEND 
And finally, I want to take this opportunity to reassure the people in this city, in this region, and Americans across our country that our counterterrorism and law enforcement professionals at every level  federal, state and local  are working together, around the clock, to prevent attacks and to keep us safe ENDEND  They are the best of the best ENDEND  Over the years, they have thwarted many plots and saved many lives ENDEND  And we are incredibly grateful for their service, today and every single day ENDEND 
We will continue to lead the global coalition in the fight to destroy ISIL, which is instigating a lot of people over the Internet to carry out attacks ENDEND  We are going to continue to go after them ENDEND  We're going to take out their leaders ENDEND  We're going to take out their infrastructure ENDEND  They are continuing to lose ground in Iraq and in Syria ENDEND  And later today, I’ll be meeting with Prime Minister Abadi of Iraq to discuss the need to sustain that momentum ENDEND  As we take away more of their territory, it exposes ISIL as the failed cause that it is ENDEND  And it helps to undermine their ideology, which over time will make it harder for them to recruit and inspire people to violence ENDEND  And we're going to continue to enlist tech companies and community and religious leaders to push back against online extremist content and all messages of hate ENDEND 
At moments like this, I think it’s important to remember what terrorists and violent extremists are trying to do ENDEND  They are trying to hurt innocent people, but they also want to inspire fear in all of us, and disrupt the way we live, to undermine our values ENDEND  And so, even as we have to be vigilant and aggressive, both in preventing senseless acts of violence but also making sure that we find those who carry out such acts and bring them to justice, we all have a role to play as citizens in making sure that we don’t succumb to that fear ENDEND  And there’s no better example of that than the people of New York and New Jersey ENDEND 
When I was speaking to Governor Cuomo and Governor Christie and Mayor De Blasio, one point that they all made is, folks around here, they don’t get scared ENDEND  They’re tough, they’re resilient, they go about their business every single day ENDEND  And that kind of toughness and resoluteness, and a recognition that neither individuals nor organizations like ISIL can ultimately undermine our way of life, that’s the kind of strength that makes me so proud to be an American ENDEND  And that’s the kind of strength that is going to be absolutely critical not just in the days to come but in the years to come ENDEND 
By showing those who want to do us harm that they will never beat us, by showing the entire world that as Americans we do not, and never will, give in to fear, that’s going to be the most important ingredient in us defeating those who would carry our terrorist acts against us ENDEND 
Thank you very much, everybody ENDEND  And as I said, you will be receiving, I’m sure, ongoing briefings from both the FBI and local law enforcement in terms of the details of the investigation ENDEND 


Good morning ENDEND  Scripture tells us, “Let not steadfast love and faithfulness forsake you…write them on the tablet of your heart ENDEND ”
Secretary Carter, Chairman Dunford, outstanding members of our Armed Forces, and most of all, survivors of that September day and the families of those we lost  it is a great honor, once again, to be with you on this day, a day that I know is still difficult, but which reveals the love and faithfulness in your hearts and in the heart of our nation ENDEND 
We remember, and we will never forget, the nearly , beautiful lives taken from us so cruelly  including  men, women and children here, the youngest just three years old ENDEND  We honor the courage of those who put themselves in harm’s way to save people they never knew ENDEND  We come together in prayer and in gratitude for the strength that has fortified us across these  years ENDEND  And we renew the love and the faith that binds us together as one American family ENDEND 
Fifteen years may seem like a long time, but for the families who lost a piece of their heart that day, I imagine it can seem like just yesterday ENDEND  Perhaps it’s the memory of a last kiss given to a spouse, or the last goodbye to a mother or father, a sister or a brother ENDEND  We wonder how their lives might have unfolded, how their dreams might have taken shape ENDEND  And I am mindful that no words we offer, or deeds we do, can ever truly erase the pain of their absence ENDEND 
And yet, you  the survivors and families of   your “steadfast love and faithfulness” has been an inspiration to me and to our entire country ENDEND  Even as you’ve mourned, you’ve summoned the strength to carry on ENDEND  In the names of those you’ve lost, you’ve started scholarships and volunteered in your communities, and done your best to be a good neighbor and a good friend and a good citizen ENDEND  And in your grief and grace, you have reminded us that, together, there’s nothing we Americans cannot overcome ENDEND 
The question before us, as always, is: How do we preserve the legacy of those we lost? How do we live up to their example? And how do we keep their spirit alive in our own hearts?
Well, we have seen the answer in a generation of Americans  our men and women in uniform, diplomats, intelligence, homeland security and law enforcement professionals  all who have stepped forward to serve and who have risked and given their lives to help keep us safe ENDEND  Thanks to their extraordinary service, we’ve dealt devastating blows to al Qaeda ENDEND 
We've delivered justice to Osama bin Laden ENDEND  We’ve strengthened our homeland security ENDEND  We've prevented attacks ENDEND  We've saved lives ENDEND  We resolve to continue doing everything in our power to protect this country that we love ENDEND  And today, we once again pay tribute to these patriots, both military and civilian, who serve in our name, including those far away from home in Afghanistan and Iraq ENDEND 
Perhaps most of all, we stay true to the spirit of this day by defending not only our country, but also our ideals ENDEND  Fifteen years into this fight, the threat has evolved ENDEND  With our stronger defenses, terrorists often attempt attacks on a smaller, but still deadly, scale ENDEND  Hateful ideologies urge people in their own country to commit unspeakable violence ENDEND  We’ve mourned the loss of innocents from Boston to San Bernardino to Orlando ENDEND 
Groups like al Qaeda, like ISIL, know that we will never be able  they will never be able to defeat a nation as great and as strong as America ENDEND  So, instead, they've tried to terrorize in the hopes that they can stoke enough fear that we turn on each other and that we change who we are or how we live ENDEND  And that's why it is so important today that we reaffirm our character as a nation  a people drawn from every corner of the world, every color, every religion, every background  bound by a creed as old as our founding, e pluribus unum ENDEND  Out of many, we are one ENDEND  For we know that our diversity  our patchwork heritage  is not a weakness; it is still, and always will be, one of our greatest strengths ENDEND  This is the America that was attacked that September morning ENDEND  This is the America that we must remain true to ENDEND 
Across our country today, Americans are coming together in service and remembrance ENDEND  We run our fingers over the names in memorial benches here at the Pentagon ENDEND  We walk the hallowed grounds of a Pennsylvania field ENDEND  We look up at a gleaming tower that pierces the New York City skyline ENDEND  But in the end, the most enduring memorial to those we lost is ensuring the America that we continue to be  that we stay true to ourselves, that we stay true to what's best in us, that we do not let others divide us ENDEND 
As I mark this solemn day with you for the last time as President, I think of Americans whose stories I’ve been humbled to know these past eight years  Americans who, I believe, embody the true spirit of  ENDEND 
It’s the courage of Welles Crowther, just  years old, in the South tower  the man in the red bandana who spent his final moments helping strangers to safety before the towers fell ENDEND  It’s the resilience of the firehouse on Eighth Avenue  patriots who lost more than a dozen men, but who still suit up every day as the “Pride of Midtown ENDEND ” It’s the love of a daughter  Payton Wall of New Jersey  whose father, in his last moments on the phone from the towers, told her, “I will always be watching over you ENDEND ”
It’s the resolve of those Navy SEALS who made sure justice was finally done, who served as we must live as a nation  getting each other’s backs, looking out for each other, united, one mission, one team ENDEND  It’s the ultimate sacrifice of men and women who rest for eternity not far from here, in gentle green hills in perfect formation  Americans who gave their lives in faraway places so that we can be here today, strong and free and proud ENDEND  It’s all of us  every American who gets up each day, and lives our lives, carries on ENDEND  Because as Americans, we do not give in to fear ENDEND  We will preserve our freedoms and the way of life that makes us a beacon to the world ENDEND 
“Let not steadfast love and faithfulness forsake you…write them on the tablet of your heart ENDEND ” And how we conduct ourselves as individuals and as a nation, we have the opportunity each and every day to live up to the sacrifice of those heroes that we lost ENDEND  May God bless the memory of the loved ones here and across the country ENDEND  They remain in our hearts today ENDEND 
May He watch over these faithful families and all who protect us ENDEND 
And may God forever bless the United States of America ENDEND
